## 3. Per sub-group detail

### BOUNDARY

_77 rows_

#### a. New VCGs derived (from v2)

| Code | Title | Verses |
|---|---|---:|
| `VCG-A-14` | sofos / sofia: human wisdom overturned by the cross | 2 |
| `VCG-A-15` | sofia: wisdom hidden in Christ and given from above | 1 |
| `VCG-A-16` | sofia: wisdom that has the appearance but not the substance | 1 |
| `VCG-B-01` | Reasoned discourse as engagement of the inner life: dialegō | 11 |
| `VCG-B-02` | The word as inner-dwelling and conscience-addressing reality: logos (1171-001 uses only) | 9 |
| `VCG-B-03` | Conscious inner awareness: suneidō as moral complicity and cognitive recognition | 3 |
| `VCG-B-04` | Interpretive capacity as expression of inner wisdom: pe.sher | 1 |
| `VCG-B-05` | Intimate teaching-to-walk: tir.gal as tender, unrecognised nurture | 1 |
| `VCG-B-06` | Translation revealing the inner theological meaning of a name: methermēneuō | 1 |
| `VCG-B-07` | Outward insistence arising from inner conviction: diabebaioō | 2 |
| `VCG-B-08` | Simile characterising an inner state: eikō | 2 |
| `VCG-B-09` | Inner habituation through training: gumnazō forming the person toward godliness or vice | 4 |
| `VCG-B-10` | Spirit-given interpretation as a community inner-life building gift: hermēneia and diermēneutēs | 3 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-A-14** — _Human wisdom as a category that the cross renders inadequate, foolish, and subject to divine judgment. God hides revelation from the wise and reveals it to children. The wisdom of the world is folly before God._
- **VCG-A-15** — _Divine wisdom as the content of what God has hidden in Christ and gives as a gift — the alternative to human wisdom, with named qualities, Spirit-given, belonging to God and the Lamb._
- **VCG-A-16** — _A named false wisdom — earthly, unspiritual, demonic — that looks like wisdom but does not come from above. Opposed to the wisdom from above._
- **VCG-B-01** — _Paul's method of reasoning in synagogues and public venues — persuasive discourse aimed at reaching and convincing the inner person. The goal is inner persuasion; the form is reasoned argument. The effect can be conviction (Felix alarmed), communal growth, or stubborn resistance._
- **VCG-B-02** — _The logos in these uses is not merely speech but a word that acts within and upon the inner person — dwelling, addressing the conscience, summing the law, revealing inner condition, evaluated by its inner power._
- **VCG-B-03** — _The same inner faculty of conscious awareness operates in two registers: (a) moral co-knowing — the inner awareness of shared participation in a morally charged act; and (b) cognitive recognition — becoming aware of a situation and acting on it._
- **VCG-B-04** — _A single verse. Knowing the interpretation of a thing is named as the mark of the wise person — the inner wisdom that discerns meaning. The wisdom is so thoroughgoing that it reshapes the outward bearing._
- **VCG-B-05** — _A single verse. God teaching Ephraim to walk — the intimate relational dynamic of the caring parent taking up the child's arms. The pathos is that the one taught did not know who healed them._
- **VCG-B-06** — _The act of translation that discloses what a name means at its theological core — Immanuel meaning God-with-us._
- **VCG-B-07** — _The act of asserting or insisting with confidence — the outward form of settled inner certainty. The two uses both name insistence without adequate inner grounding (first use) or with proper grounding (second use)._
- **VCG-B-08** — _The simile reveals what an inner condition is like — the comparison illuminates the nature of inner instability or unreceptive hearing._
- **VCG-B-09** — _The inner person is formed through repeated practice — the same mechanism (habitual exercise) produces either godliness and discernment (positive) or greed (negative). The inner disposition is trainable in both directions._
- **VCG-B-10** — _The Spirit-given capacity to interpret tongues — enabling what is spoken in tongues to become intelligible inner content for the community. Without interpretation, tongues cannot build up the inner life of others; only private inner communion with God remains._

#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `1080-001` → `VCG-B-01` (11 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the act of reasoning and disputing as an engagement of inner faculties — where discourse aims to persuade, convince, or address the inner life of hearers, or expresses inner orientation
- **NEW** (Reasoned discourse as engagement of the inner life: dialegō): Paul's method of reasoning in synagogues and public venues — persuasive discourse aimed at reaching and convincing the inner person. The goal is inner persuasion; the form is reasoned argument. The effect can be conviction (Felix alarmed), communal growth, or stubborn resistance.
- _Sample verse:_ Mar 9:34 (G1256)

##### `1171-001` → `VCG-B-02` (9 verses)

- **DB**: The word as inner-dwelling and conscience-addressing — the word of Christ taking up residence within, addressing the conscience, or expressing/revealing the inner being of the person
- **NEW** (The word as inner-dwelling and conscience-addressing reality: logos (1171-001 uses only)): The logos in these uses is not merely speech but a word that acts within and upon the inner person — dwelling, addressing the conscience, summing the law, revealing inner condition, evaluated by its inner power.
- _Sample verse:_ Rom 13:9 (G3056)

##### `454-001` → `VCG-B-03` (3 verses)

- **DB**: Term names a conscious inner awareness — moral complicity or cognitive recognition — that informs volitional response. The moral-complicity pole (shared inner co-knowing of one's participation in a morally charged act) is the primary conscience characteristic; the cognitive-recognition pole (becoming aware of a situation) represents the term's broader semantic range within the same faculty.
- **NEW** (Conscious inner awareness: suneidō as moral complicity and cognitive recognition): The same inner faculty of conscious awareness operates in two registers: (a) moral co-knowing — the inner awareness of shared participation in a morally charged act; and (b) cognitive recognition — becoming aware of a situation and acting on it.
- _Sample verse:_ Act 5:2 (G4894)

##### `7419-001` → `VCG-B-09` (3 verses)

- **DB**: Term describes the inner training of the person toward spiritual maturity — habituating discernment, righteousness, and godliness
- **NEW** (Inner habituation through training: gumnazō forming the person toward godliness or vice): The inner person is formed through repeated practice — the same mechanism (habitual exercise) produces either godliness and discernment (positive) or greed (negative). The inner disposition is trainable in both directions.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Ti 4:7 (G1128)

##### `(none)` → `VCG-A-14` (2 verses)

- **DB**: _(no DB description)_
- **NEW** (sofos / sofia: human wisdom overturned by the cross): Human wisdom as a category that the cross renders inadequate, foolish, and subject to divine judgment. God hides revelation from the wise and reveals it to children. The wisdom of the world is folly before God.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 2:1 (G3056)

##### `5864-001` → `VCG-B-10` (2 verses)

- **DB**: Term names interpretation as a Spirit-given inner capacity — a gift enabling the community to understand and be built up
- **NEW** (Spirit-given interpretation as a community inner-life building gift: hermēneia and diermēneutēs): The Spirit-given capacity to interpret tongues — enabling what is spoken in tongues to become intelligible inner content for the community. Without interpretation, tongues cannot build up the inner life of others; only private inner communion with God remains.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 12:10 (G2058)

##### `7085-001` → `VCG-B-07` (2 verses)

- **DB**: Diabebaioō as outward insistence arising from inner conviction
- **NEW** (Outward insistence arising from inner conviction: diabebaioō): The act of asserting or insisting with confidence — the outward form of settled inner certainty. The two uses both name insistence without adequate inner grounding (first use) or with proper grounding (second use).
- _Sample verse:_ 1Ti 1:7 (G1226)

##### `7333-001` → `VCG-B-08` (2 verses)

- **DB**: Term frames a simile that characterises an inner state — self-deception or inner instability
- **NEW** (Simile characterising an inner state: eikō): The simile reveals what an inner condition is like — the comparison illuminates the nature of inner instability or unreceptive hearing.
- _Sample verse:_ Jam 1:6 (G1503)

##### `(none)` → `VCG-A-15` (1 verses)

- **DB**: _(no DB description)_
- **NEW** (sofia: wisdom hidden in Christ and given from above): Divine wisdom as the content of what God has hidden in Christ and gives as a gift — the alternative to human wisdom, with named qualities, Spirit-given, belonging to God and the Lamb.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 12:8 (G3056)

##### `(none)` → `VCG-A-16` (1 verses)

- **DB**: _(no DB description)_
- **NEW** (sofia: wisdom that has the appearance but not the substance): A named false wisdom — earthly, unspiritual, demonic — that looks like wisdom but does not come from above. Opposed to the wisdom from above.
- _Sample verse:_ Col 2:23 (G3056)

##### `5865-001` → `VCG-B-10` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the interpreter whose absence requires the speaker to keep inner communion with God rather than public expression
- **NEW** (Spirit-given interpretation as a community inner-life building gift: hermēneia and diermēneutēs): The Spirit-given capacity to interpret tongues — enabling what is spoken in tongues to become intelligible inner content for the community. Without interpretation, tongues cannot build up the inner life of others; only private inner communion with God remains.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 14:28 (G1328)

##### `6085-001` → `VCG-B-04` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the interpretive capacity as an expression of inner wisdom — the ability to discern meaning is a quality of the inner person whose wisdom transforms even outward bearing
- **NEW** (Interpretive capacity as expression of inner wisdom: pe.sher): A single verse. Knowing the interpretation of a thing is named as the mark of the wise person — the inner wisdom that discerns meaning. The wisdom is so thoroughgoing that it reshapes the outward bearing.
- _Sample verse:_ Ecc 8:1 (H6592)

##### `6256-001` → `VCG-B-05` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the intimate act of teaching to walk — evoking the inner-relational dynamic between the caring teacher-parent and the dependent learner, with the poignancy of unrecognised nurture
- **NEW** (Intimate teaching-to-walk: tir.gal as tender, unrecognised nurture): A single verse. God teaching Ephraim to walk — the intimate relational dynamic of the caring parent taking up the child's arms. The pathos is that the one taught did not know who healed them.
- _Sample verse:_ Hos 11:3 (H8637)

##### `7419-002` → `VCG-B-09` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term describes the inner habituation of the heart toward vice — the trained disposition toward greed
- **NEW** (Inner habituation through training: gumnazō forming the person toward godliness or vice): The inner person is formed through repeated practice — the same mechanism (habitual exercise) produces either godliness and discernment (positive) or greed (negative). The inner disposition is trainable in both directions.
- _Sample verse:_ 2Pe 2:14 (G1128)

##### `973-001` → `VCG-B-06` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names translation that reveals the theological heart of a name — Immanuel as the inner meaning of God's incarnate presence
- **NEW** (Translation revealing the inner theological meaning of a name: methermēneuō): The act of translation that discloses what a name means at its theological core — Immanuel meaning God-with-us.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 1:23 (G3177)

### M15-A

_298 rows_

#### a. New VCGs derived (from v2)

| Code | Title | Verses |
|---|---|---:|
| `VCG-A-01` | Wisdom as constituted inner quality of character: cha.kham as holistic inner endowment | 44 |
| `VCG-A-02` | Wisdom as governance qualification: cha.kham as inner capacity required for leadership | 12 |
| `VCG-A-03` | Professional court wise men as institutional class: cha.kham / chak.kim as class title | 15 |
| `VCG-A-04` | Wisdom receiving instruction and growing: cha.kham as receptive and cumulative | 1 |
| `VCG-A-05` | Self-attributed wisdom: cha.kham as false inner claim | 14 |
| `VCG-A-06` | Wisdom destroyed or absent in judgment: cha.kham as what God removes | 4 |
| `VCG-A-07` | Sacred craft wisdom: cha.kham and cha.shav H2803G as God-given inner capacity for sacred construction | 24 |
| `VCG-A-08` | Craft skill applied to secular or non-sacred purposes: cha.kham and cha.shav in craft outside the sanctuary | 7 |
| `VCG-A-09` | cha.shav H2803G as evil devising: scheming against persons | 3 |
| `VCG-A-10` | cha.shav H2803G as divine purposive devising: forming a means of mercy | 1 |
| `VCG-A-11` | tu.shiy.yah: sound wisdom as effective inner resource | 11 |
| `VCG-A-12` | se.khel: discernment as personal inner quality producing good outcomes | 15 |
| `VCG-A-13` | Aramaic wisdom terms: chokh.mah / chak.kim as divine wisdom given to Daniel | 8 |
| `VCG-A-14` | sofos / sofia: human wisdom overturned by the cross | 18 |
| `VCG-A-15` | sofia: wisdom hidden in Christ and given from above | 17 |
| `VCG-A-16` | sofia: wisdom that has the appearance but not the substance | 2 |
| `VCG-A-17` | sofia as the mode of proclamation and instruction | 3 |
| `VCG-A-18` | fronimos: practical shrewd wisdom expressed in action and stewardship | 5 |
| `VCG-A-19` | froneō: the inner orientation of the mind set on divine or earthly things | 2 |
| `VCG-A-20` | froneō: relational concern and communal alignment | 9 |
| `VCG-A-21` | sofizo: making wise (positive) and devising myths (negative) | 2 |
| `VCG-B-01` | bin / bi.nah as constituted inner perceptive faculty: understanding governing speech, relationships, and perception | 1 |
| `VCG-B-02` | Understanding as governance qualification: bin / bi.nah as what leadership requires | 1 |
| `VCG-B-07` | Judicial withholding of understanding: suniēmi / bin as blocked comprehension | 1 |
| `VCG-B-16` | sunetos / asunetos: the intelligent/discerning person excluded from divine disclosure; or the foolish excluded from wisdom | 1 |
| `VCG-C-01` | da.at as inner possession: knowledge as an inner quality of the wise person | 3 |
| `VCG-D-06` | a.rum / a.rom: prudent inner disposition as perceptive self-governance | 1 |
| `VCG-E-01` | Human counsel: wisdom given between persons shaping deliberation | 1 |
| `VCG-E-04` | Divine counsel: God's sovereign purposive intent directed toward nations and history | 1 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-A-01** — _Wisdom as a defining inner quality of the person — not a skill or technique but a whole-person orientation that shows in perception, speech, conduct, and relationships. The quality is positive and characterises those who are genuinely wise._
- **VCG-A-02** — _Wisdom as the specific qualification needed for the exercise of leadership and governance — it is the inner quality that enables just rule, right appointments, and effective governance._
- **VCG-A-03** — _The court class of professional wise men — summoned for interpretation, giving counsel, named as the foil for what Spirit-given wisdom can do. Their title and incapacity stand together in the Daniel narratives._
- **VCG-A-04** — _The wise person's inner quality makes them open to instruction, correction, and growth — wisdom receives and is enriched. Opposed to the fool who trusts only their own judgment._
- **VCG-A-05** — _Persons who attribute wisdom to themselves without having it — the inner claim is exposed as false, hollow, or dangerous._
- **VCG-A-06** — _God destroys, removes, or withholds wisdom from those who rely on it against him — the wise men of nations are rendered helpless, made fools, or destroyed._
- **VCG-A-07** — _The inner capacity for skilled design and execution, explicitly God-given (filled with a spirit of skill), directed toward the construction of sacred objects and spaces. Both cha.kham (the persons) and cha.shav (the designing/executing) are included._
- **VCG-A-08** — _The same inner capacity for craft skill and design applied outside the sacred context — to ships, idols, military machines, and instruments of music._
- **VCG-A-09** — _The same inner devising capacity directed toward harm — plotting, scheming, purposing destruction against persons or groups. Confirmed as distinct from sacred craft use._
- **VCG-A-10** — _A single verse. God devises means so that the banished one will not remain an outcast — this is divine inner purposing directed toward a merciful outcome, not craft design or human scheming._
- **VCG-A-11** — _Sound wisdom as a substantial, effective inner capacity — held by God, available to the upright, able to sustain and protect, violated by isolation, equated with the fear of God._
- **VCG-A-12** — _A distinctive inner quality of practical wisdom — discernment, good sense, shrewd perception — that produces favourable outcomes and is recognisable in persons._
- **VCG-A-13** — _Wisdom as God's exclusive gift — given to Daniel, belonging to God, not a product of professional training. The Aramaic terms operate consistently in the Daniel narratives as marking the contrast between institutional wisdom (which fails) and Spirit-given wisdom (which succeeds)._
- **VCG-A-14** — _Human wisdom as a category that the cross renders inadequate, foolish, and subject to divine judgment. God hides revelation from the wise and reveals it to children. The wisdom of the world is folly before God._
- **VCG-A-15** — _Divine wisdom as the content of what God has hidden in Christ and gives as a gift — the alternative to human wisdom, with named qualities, Spirit-given, belonging to God and the Lamb._
- **VCG-A-16** — _A named false wisdom — earthly, unspiritual, demonic — that looks like wisdom but does not come from above. Opposed to the wisdom from above._
- **VCG-A-17** — _Wisdom as the inner quality that shapes how the gospel and community teaching are offered — the wise way of walking toward outsiders, teaching with wisdom, admonishing with wisdom._
- **VCG-A-18** — _The inner quality of practical wisdom that shows in foresighted action — preparation for what is needed, trustworthy stewardship in the master's absence, shrewd navigation of a hostile world._
- **VCG-A-19** — _The habitual inner direction of the whole person — what the mind is set on. The command is to set the mind on things above; the warning is against setting it on earthly or self-oriented things._
- **VCG-A-20** — _The inner orientation directed toward another person or the community — attention, care, shared mind, alignment in conflict resolution._
- **VCG-A-21** — _Two opposite uses of the same term — one naming Scripture's transformative work of making the person wise for salvation; the other naming what the apostles explicitly did not do (devise clever myths)._
- **VCG-B-01** — _Understanding as a substantive inner quality of the person — what they are characterised by. The faculty is active, receptive, and productive: it governs what the wise person perceives, how they speak, and how they relate. The person of understanding is defined by this quality._
- **VCG-B-02** — _Understanding paired with wisdom as the inner quality that qualifies persons for governance, judgment, and appointments. The capacity to discern rightly between situations, persons, and cases._
- **VCG-B-07** — _Understanding deliberately withheld by God — the inner faculty is present but its activation is prevented by divine judgment. Hearing without receiving; perception without comprehension._
- **VCG-B-16** — _Intelligence/discernment as a human category — which the cross reverses, from which divine mysteries are hidden, or which is commended as openness to the word._
- **VCG-C-01** — _Knowledge as what the wise person holds inwardly — the inner capacity/content that Proverbs aims to produce, that the wise accumulate and guard, and that gives the person strength._
- **VCG-D-06** — _The inner quality of prudence in the sense of perceptive self-governance — seeing situations clearly and governing speech and conduct with care. Directionally neutral: serves righteousness (Proverbs uses) or deception (Gen 3:1, Job 15:5)._
- **VCG-E-01** — _One person gives advice or counsel to another — the inner wisdom of the advisor expressed and offered to shape the recipient's purposes. The outcome depends on whether counsel is received or rejected._
- **VCG-E-04** — _God forms and executes sovereign intention that cannot be annulled or redirected. His counsel is self-originating, irresistible, and encompasses the whole of history. Multiple human terms (ya.ats, cha.shav, za.mam) converge in expressing this._

#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `528-001` → `VCG-A-01` (42 verses)

- **DB**: cha.kham in Proverbs, Ecclesiastes, and historical narrative names wisdom as a constituted inner quality of the person — not a role or a skill but who they are. The wise person is characterised by this quality: they receive instruction, they are cautious, they hold back their spirit, their heart is in the right place. The quality is relational — it shows in how they relate to others, to rebuke, to advice.
- **NEW** (Wisdom as constituted inner quality of character: cha.kham as holistic inner endowment): Wisdom as a defining inner quality of the person — not a skill or technique but a whole-person orientation that shows in perception, speech, conduct, and relationships. The quality is positive and characterises those who are genuinely wise.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 49:10 (H2450)

##### `528-004` → `VCG-A-07` (22 verses)

- **DB**: cha.kham and cha.shav H2803G name an inner capacity for skilled craft that is explicitly Spirit-given. The skill resides in the heart/mind and is directed toward sacred construction. This is not general competence — it is an endowment for holy work.
- **NEW** (Sacred craft wisdom: cha.kham and cha.shav H2803G as God-given inner capacity for sacred construction): The inner capacity for skilled design and execution, explicitly God-given (filled with a spirit of skill), directed toward the construction of sacred objects and spaces. Both cha.kham (the persons) and cha.shav (the designing/executing) are included.
- _Sample verse:_ Exo 28:3 (H2450)

##### `4458-001` → `VCG-A-14` (15 verses)

- **DB**: sofia and sofos in 1 Corinthians 1–3, and in parallel passages, name human wisdom as a category that the cross overturns. God hides things from the wise; the wisdom of the world is folly with God. This is not wisdom inverted by the person claiming it (A-4) but wisdom as a category that stands in structural opposition to the wisdom of God.
- **NEW** (sofos / sofia: human wisdom overturned by the cross): Human wisdom as a category that the cross renders inadequate, foolish, and subject to divine judgment. God hides revelation from the wise and reveals it to children. The wisdom of the world is folly before God.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 1:19 (G4678)

##### `525-001` → `VCG-A-12` (15 verses)

- **DB**: se.khel names a practical inner quality of good sense, prudence, and wise conduct. It produces outcomes — favour, success, slow anger. It can be given (1Ch 22:12), recognised (1Sa 25:3), or taught (Neh 8:8). Its absence closes hearts (Job 17:4). It has a dark use (Dan 8:25 — cunning serving deceit).
- **NEW** (se.khel: discernment as personal inner quality producing good outcomes): A distinctive inner quality of practical wisdom — discernment, good sense, shrewd perception — that produces favourable outcomes and is recognisable in persons.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Sa 25:3 (H7922)

##### `527-001` → `VCG-A-11` (11 verses)

- **DB**: tu.shiy.yah names wisdom in its effectiveness — sound wisdom, effective knowledge, the capacity to produce good outcomes. It can be God's attribute (with him is sound wisdom) or a human resource (keep sound wisdom). Reading the verses shows these are the same characteristic in different registers, not two separate groups.
- **NEW** (tu.shiy.yah: sound wisdom as effective inner resource): Sound wisdom as a substantial, effective inner capacity — held by God, available to the upright, able to sustain and protect, violated by isolation, equated with the fear of God.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 5:12 (H8454)

##### `532-002` → `VCG-A-15` (10 verses)

- **DB**: Wisdom as a gift — God gives it, persons receive it, it enables what the recipient could not produce from themselves. The giving and receiving is the characteristic dynamic of this group.
- **NEW** (sofia: wisdom hidden in Christ and given from above): Divine wisdom as the content of what God has hidden in Christ and gives as a gift — the alternative to human wisdom, with named qualities, Spirit-given, belonging to God and the Lamb.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 2:6 (G4678)

##### `528-005` → `VCG-A-03` (9 verses)

- **DB**: cha.kham here names wisdom as the qualification for a role — the wise man sought for appointment, the wise men of the court, those who have the inner capacity for governance, law, and counsel. The focus is on wisdom as a capacity that qualifies persons for institutional responsibility.
- **NEW** (Professional court wise men as institutional class: cha.kham / chak.kim as class title): The court class of professional wise men — summoned for interpretation, giving counsel, named as the foil for what Spirit-given wisdom can do. Their title and incapacity stand together in the Daniel narratives.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 41:8 (H2450)

##### `996-001` → `VCG-A-20` (9 verses)

- **DB**: froneō does not name a single faculty but the orientation of the whole inner person — what one is set on, caring about, thinking about as a habitual posture. The Philippians verses are central: "have this mind which is in Christ Jesus" is the paradigmatic use. Reading the verses, 1825 (mind on divine vs earthly) and 1826 (relational/communal mindedness) are two expressions of the same characteristic: froneō as the inner orientation of the whole person, directed toward an object. They belong in one group.
- **NEW** (froneō: relational concern and communal alignment): The inner orientation directed toward another person or the community — attention, care, shared mind, alignment in conflict resolution.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 13:11 (G5426)

##### `528-003` → `VCG-A-05` (7 verses)

- **DB**: cha.kham here names wisdom turned back on itself — the person who claims wisdom without the fear of the Lord, whose wisdom serves evil, or whose self-assessment of wisdom is the very sign of its absence.
- **NEW** (Self-attributed wisdom: cha.kham as false inner claim): Persons who attribute wisdom to themselves without having it — the inner claim is exposed as false, hollow, or dangerous.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 32:6 (H2450)

##### `528-001` → `VCG-A-05` (6 verses)

- **DB**: cha.kham in Proverbs, Ecclesiastes, and historical narrative names wisdom as a constituted inner quality of the person — not a role or a skill but who they are. The wise person is characterised by this quality: they receive instruction, they are cautious, they hold back their spirit, their heart is in the right place. The quality is relational — it shows in how they relate to others, to rebuke, to advice.
- **NEW** (Self-attributed wisdom: cha.kham as false inner claim): Persons who attribute wisdom to themselves without having it — the inner claim is exposed as false, hollow, or dangerous.
- _Sample verse:_ Judg 5:29 (H2450)

##### `528-004` → `VCG-A-08` (6 verses)

- **DB**: cha.kham and cha.shav H2803G name an inner capacity for skilled craft that is explicitly Spirit-given. The skill resides in the heart/mind and is directed toward sacred construction. This is not general competence — it is an endowment for holy work.
- **NEW** (Craft skill applied to secular or non-sacred purposes: cha.kham and cha.shav in craft outside the sanctuary): The same inner capacity for craft skill and design applied outside the sacred context — to ships, idols, military machines, and instruments of music.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Ch 22:15 (H2450)

##### `528-005` → `VCG-A-02` (6 verses)

- **DB**: cha.kham here names wisdom as the qualification for a role — the wise man sought for appointment, the wise men of the court, those who have the inner capacity for governance, law, and counsel. The focus is on wisdom as a capacity that qualifies persons for institutional responsibility.
- **NEW** (Wisdom as governance qualification: cha.kham as inner capacity required for leadership): Wisdom as the specific qualification needed for the exercise of leadership and governance — it is the inner quality that enables just rule, right appointments, and effective governance.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 1:13 (H2450)

##### `6668-001` → `VCG-A-03` (6 verses)

- **DB**: The chak.kim P-status verses all appear in Daniel 2–5. They name "the wise men of Babylon" — the institutional class of court wise men who cannot read divine mysteries. They form the consistent foil: what human wisdom (even at its most professional and prestigious) cannot do, the Spirit-given wisdom in Daniel can. The group's function is structural contrast — it makes visible what Spirit-given wisdom is by showing what it is not.
- **NEW** (Professional court wise men as institutional class: cha.kham / chak.kim as class title): The court class of professional wise men — summoned for interpretation, giving counsel, named as the foil for what Spirit-given wisdom can do. Their title and incapacity stand together in the Daniel narratives.
- _Sample verse:_ Dan 2:12 (H2445)

##### `3459-001` → `VCG-A-18` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Shrewdness as an inner quality of practical wisdom — the capacity for perceptive, pragmatic discernment in worldly dealings, commended even when applied by those without spiritual orientation (Luk 16:8).
- **NEW** (fronimos: practical shrewd wisdom expressed in action and stewardship): The inner quality of practical wisdom that shows in foresighted action — preparation for what is needed, trustworthy stewardship in the master's absence, shrewd navigation of a hostile world.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 7:24 (G5429)

##### `532-002` → `VCG-A-13` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Wisdom as a gift — God gives it, persons receive it, it enables what the recipient could not produce from themselves. The giving and receiving is the characteristic dynamic of this group.
- **NEW** (Aramaic wisdom terms: chokh.mah / chak.kim as divine wisdom given to Daniel): Wisdom as God's exclusive gift — given to Daniel, belonging to God, not a product of professional training. The Aramaic terms operate consistently in the Daniel narratives as marking the contrast between institutional wisdom (which fails) and Spirit-given wisdom (which succeeds).
- _Sample verse:_ Ezr 7:25 (H2452)

##### `4458-001` → `VCG-A-07` (2 verses)

This is not wisdom inverted by the person claiming it (A-4) but wisdom as a category that stands in structural opposition to the wisdom of God.

| `VCG-B-17` | fronesis: practical wisdom / moral orientation as divine gift | 1 |
| `VCG-B-18` | epistēmōn: genuine knowing verified by conduct | 1 |
| `VCG-C-03` | da.at as instrument of divine work and Spirit-endowment | 1 |
| `VCG-C-04` | da.at as absent in the foolish and hollow | 1 |
| `VCG-C-07` | ya.da as the "then you shall know" pattern: divine self-disclosure through event producing recognition | 1 |
| `VCG-C-10` | ya.da as moral knowledge guiding right action | 1 |
| `VCG-C-12` | ya.da as limits of human knowing before divine mystery | 1 |
| `VCG-C-13` | de.ah as the knowledge of the Lord filling the earth: eschatological covenantal knowing | 1 |
| `VCG-D-03` | Evaluative regard of persons and things: assigning worth or category by reckoning | 1 |
| `VCG-D-05` | sa.khal as perceptive prudent discernment: seeing clearly what is before you | 4 |
| `VCG-D-06` | a.rum / a.rom: prudent inner disposition as perceptive self-governance | 2 |
| `VCG-E-01` | Human counsel: wisdom given between persons shaping deliberation | 1 |
| `VCG-F-02` | Meditative dwelling on God's law, precepts, and word: si.ach as law-meditation | 1 |
| `VCG-F-07` | Heart-meditation producing understanding: ha.gut as the contemplative inner engagement | 1 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-A-01** — _Wisdom as a defining inner quality of the person — not a skill or technique but a whole-person orientation that shows in perception, speech, conduct, and relationships. The quality is positive and characterises those who are genuinely wise._
- **VCG-A-08** — _The same inner capacity for craft skill and design applied outside the sacred context — to ships, idols, military machines, and instruments of music._
- **VCG-A-12** — _A distinctive inner quality of practical wisdom — discernment, good sense, shrewd perception — that produces favourable outcomes and is recognisable in persons._
- **VCG-A-13** — _Wisdom as God's exclusive gift — given to Daniel, belonging to God, not a product of professional training. The Aramaic terms operate consistently in the Daniel narratives as marking the contrast between institutional wisdom (which fails) and Spirit-given wisdom (which succeeds)._
- **VCG-A-14** — _Human wisdom as a category that the cross renders inadequate, foolish, and subject to divine judgment. God hides revelation from the wise and reveals it to children. The wisdom of the world is folly before God._
- **VCG-B-01** — _Understanding as a substantive inner quality of the person — what they are characterised by. The faculty is active, receptive, and productive: it governs what the wise person perceives, how they speak, and how they relate. The person of understanding is defined by this quality._
- **VCG-B-02** — _Understanding paired with wisdom as the inner quality that qualifies persons for governance, judgment, and appointments. The capacity to discern rightly between situations, persons, and cases._
- **VCG-B-03** — _Understanding as explicitly God-given — the inner capacity placed within the person by God or the Spirit, not acquired through human effort. Includes craft intelligence for sacred work and the Messiah's Spirit-given understanding._
- **VCG-B-04** — _Understanding as the fruit of deliberate orientation toward God — seeking, keeping the precepts, holding to the covenant. The faculty grows and deepens through the person's active engagement._
- **VCG-B-05** — _God's inner perceptive faculty directed toward the human person — his understanding of thoughts, deeds, plans, and the heart. Divine understanding of the human is comprehensive and intimate._
- **VCG-B-06** — _Understanding absent in persons or groups — whether through their own failure, the consequence of wickedness, the absence of the divine gift, or Israel's characteristic blindness._
- **VCG-B-07** — _Understanding deliberately withheld by God — the inner faculty is present but its activation is prevented by divine judgment. Hearing without receiving; perception without comprehension._
- **VCG-B-08** — _The positive activation of the inner perceptive faculty — Christ opening minds, understanding breaking through, the disciples receiving what had previously been closed to them._
- **VCG-B-09** — _The total absence of inner understanding in fallen humanity — not a specific judicial act but a description of the general human condition before God._
- **VCG-B-10** — _The person exercises the inner perceptive faculty but reaches its boundary — divine works, cosmic scale, the mystery of God's ways are simply beyond human comprehension._
- **VCG-B-11** — _Bin used in the sense of directing perceptive attention toward something — looking closely, examining carefully, paying attention. Distinct from understanding as comprehension. The faculty is directed attention, not cognitive grasping._
- **VCG-B-12** — _Understanding as a property of God himself — the attribute by which he made the heavens and subdued chaos. Self-originating and infinite._
- **VCG-B-13** — _Understanding as an inner quality that benefits its possessor — protective, life-giving, associated with maturity and long experience._
- **VCG-B-14** — _The same inner capacity applied outside the sacred context — to idol-making or self-enrichment. The term is directionally neutral; its object determines its moral valence._
- **VCG-B-15** — _The inner comprehension of what was hidden — the mystery of Christ, the mystery of God's will — given as a divine endowment, not acquired by human intelligence._
- **VCG-B-16** — _Intelligence/discernment as a human category — which the cross reverses, from which divine mysteries are hidden, or which is commended as openness to the word._
- **VCG-B-17** — _Practical insight as a divine endowment — enabling recognition of God's will, naming the moral orientation of the just, shaping the inner person toward wisdom in all things._
- **VCG-B-18** — _A single verse. Genuine knowing as an inner quality that must be demonstrated through conduct — not claimed but shown in meekness and good works._
- **VCG-C-03** — _Knowledge as a Spirit-given capacity; as a divine attribute; as the instrument of the Servant's justifying work. These are cases where da.at has extraordinary theological weight._
- **VCG-C-04** — _Knowledge as what is absent, empty, or distorted — speech without knowledge; wisdom that has become falsehood._
- **VCG-C-07** — _A repeated pattern across the OT: God acts, and the purpose of the action is that persons will know — know that he is the Lord, that he is present, that he sent his messenger. The knowing is produced by the event, not by the seeker._
- **VCG-C-10** — _The inner moral knowing that directs the righteous person — knowing what is acceptable, what is just, what is right. Its absence names moral blindness; its presence names moral clarity._
- **VCG-C-12** — _Human ya.da encountering its own limits before God's work, purposes, and nature — cannot comprehend, cannot find, cannot know the end or the route._
- **VCG-C-13** — _Knowledge of the Lord as the content of the eschatological promise — universal, filling, covering as the waters cover the sea._
- **VCG-D-03** — _One person (human or divine) evaluates another person, group, or thing by reckoning — assigning them a worth, category, or status. The reckoning is relational and evaluative, not judicial-moral as in VCG-D-01. Includes both positive and negative assessments, and both legitimate and contested evaluations._
- **VCG-D-05** — _The inner capacity for perceptive attending — seeing God's acts, situations, or conditions with clarity and wisdom. The prudent person considers, ponders, observes rightly where others miss or fail to attend._
- **VCG-D-06** — _The inner quality of prudence in the sense of perceptive self-governance — seeing situations clearly and governing speech and conduct with care. Directionally neutral: serves righteousness (Proverbs uses) or deception (Gen 3:1, Job 15:5)._
- **VCG-E-01** — _One person gives advice or counsel to another — the inner wisdom of the advisor expressed and offered to shape the recipient's purposes. The outcome depends on whether counsel is received or rejected._
- **VCG-F-02** — _The sustained inward dwelling on God's law, precepts, statutes, and promises — the defining meditative practice of the devoted person. The object is always divine instruction. All uses from Psalm 119._
- **VCG-F-07** — _A single verse. The meditation of the heart is named as what produces understanding — the reflective inner engagement before God is the generative activity from which wisdom flows._

#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-B-01` (19 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (bin / bi.nah as constituted inner perceptive faculty: understanding governing speech, relationships, and perception): Understanding as a substantive inner quality of the person — what they are characterised by. The faculty is active, receptive, and productive: it governs what the wise person perceives, how they speak, and how they relate. The person of understanding is defined by this quality.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Ch 27:32 (H0995)

##### `523-002` → `VCG-B-04` (14 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as a human inner-being capacity — the gift from God enabling discernment of his ways and wise conduct
- **NEW** (Understanding gained through seeking and engagement with the word and covenant): Understanding as the fruit of deliberate orientation toward God — seeking, keeping the precepts, holding to the covenant. The faculty grows and deepens through the person's active engagement.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 28:12 (H0998)

##### `932-004` → `VCG-B-07` (10 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the failure, hardening, or absence of inner understanding — spiritual blindness, incapacity to perceive God or moral reality, and the rhetorical limits of human comprehension before God
- **NEW** (Judicial withholding of understanding: suniēmi / bin as blocked comprehension): Understanding deliberately withheld by God — the inner faculty is present but its activation is prevented by divine judgment. Hearing without receiving; perception without comprehension.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 13:13 (G4920)

##### `524-002` → `VCG-B-01` (9 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as a human inner-being capacity — enabling wisdom, right conduct, and discernment, received from God
- **NEW** (bin / bi.nah as constituted inner perceptive faculty: understanding governing speech, relationships, and perception): Understanding as a substantive inner quality of the person — what they are characterised by. The faculty is active, receptive, and productive: it governs what the wise person perceives, how they speak, and how they relate. The person of understanding is defined by this quality.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 10:23 (H8394)

##### `932-004` → `VCG-B-10` (8 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the failure, hardening, or absence of inner understanding — spiritual blindness, incapacity to perceive God or moral reality, and the rhetorical limits of human comprehension before God
- **NEW** (Limits of human understanding before divine mystery: bin / bi.nah facing what cannot be grasped): The person exercises the inner perceptive faculty but reaches its boundary — divine works, cosmic scale, the mystery of God's ways are simply beyond human comprehension.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 9:11 (H0995)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-B-04` (7 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (Understanding gained through seeking and engagement with the word and covenant): Understanding as the fruit of deliberate orientation toward God — seeking, keeping the precepts, holding to the covenant. The faculty grows and deepens through the person's active engagement.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 1:2 (H0995)

##### `1205-001` → `VCG-B-08` (6 verses)

- **DB**: Understanding as an inner receptive act — the mind/heart grasping revealed truth
- **NEW** (Christ opening minds to understand: suniēmi as receptive inner comprehension activated): The positive activation of the inner perceptive faculty — Christ opening minds, understanding breaking through, the disciples receiving what had previously been closed to them.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 13:23 (G4920)

##### `524-002` → `VCG-B-03` (6 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as a human inner-being capacity — enabling wisdom, right conduct, and discernment, received from God
- **NEW** (Spirit-given understanding: bin / bi.nah / te.vu.nah as a divine endowment): Understanding as explicitly God-given — the inner capacity placed within the person by God or the Spirit, not acquired through human effort. Includes craft intelligence for sacred work and the Messiah's Spirit-given understanding.
- _Sample verse:_ Exo 31:3 (H8394)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-B-02` (6 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (Understanding as governance qualification: bin / bi.nah as what leadership requires): Understanding paired with wisdom as the inner quality that qualifies persons for governance, judgment, and appointments. The capacity to discern rightly between situations, persons, and cases.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 41:33 (H0995)

##### `932-004` → `VCG-B-06` (6 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the failure, hardening, or absence of inner understanding — spiritual blindness, incapacity to perceive God or moral reality, and the rhetorical limits of human comprehension before God
- **NEW** (Failed or absent understanding: bin as the person who cannot perceive): Understanding absent in persons or groups — whether through their own failure, the consequence of wickedness, the absence of the divine gift, or Israel's characteristic blindness.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 1:3 (H0995)

##### `523-002` → `VCG-B-03` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as a human inner-being capacity — the gift from God enabling discernment of his ways and wise conduct
- **NEW** (Spirit-given understanding: bin / bi.nah / te.vu.nah as a divine endowment): Understanding as explicitly God-given — the inner capacity placed within the person by God or the Spirit, not acquired through human effort. Includes craft intelligence for sacred work and the Messiah's Spirit-given understanding.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Ch 22:12 (H0998)

##### `524-001` → `VCG-B-12` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as a divine attribute — the infinite discernment by which God creates, orders, and governs all things
- **NEW** (te.vu.nah as divine creative and governing attribute): Understanding as a property of God himself — the attribute by which he made the heavens and subdued chaos. Self-originating and infinite.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 12:13 (H8394)

##### `524-002` → `VCG-B-13` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as a human inner-being capacity — enabling wisdom, right conduct, and discernment, received from God
- **NEW** (te.vu.nah as protective and productive inner quality growing with age and experience): Understanding as an inner quality that benefits its possessor — protective, life-giving, associated with maturity and long experience.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 12:12 (H8394)

##### `932-003` → `VCG-B-05` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Term names God's inner comprehension of the human person — God's perception, understanding, and attending to the heart, thought, and deed
- **NEW** (God's perceptive comprehension of the human person: bin / bi.nah as divine knowing): God's inner perceptive faculty directed toward the human person — his understanding of thoughts, deeds, plans, and the heart. Divine understanding of the human is comprehensive and intimate.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Ch 28:9 (H0995)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-B-11` (4 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (Directional attending: bin as perceptive attention directed toward an object): Bin used in the sense of directing perceptive attention toward something — looking closely, examining carefully, paying attention. Distinct from understanding as comprehension. The faculty is directed attention, not cognitive grasping.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Ki 3:21 (H0995)

##### `932-004` → `VCG-B-11` (4 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the failure, hardening, or absence of inner understanding — spiritual blindness, incapacity to perceive God or moral reality, and the rhetorical limits of human comprehension before God

##### `1202-001` → `VCG-B-09` (3 verses)

- _Sample verse:_ Rom 1:21 (G0801)

##### `531-001` → `VCG-B-17` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as an inner-being capacity — the comprehension of God's will that enables transformed living
- **NEW** (fronesis: practical wisdom / moral orientation as divine gift): Practical insight as a divine endowment — enabling recognition of God's will, naming the moral orientation of the just, shaping the inner person toward wisdom in all things.
- _Sample verse:_ Luk 1:17 (G5428)

##### `816-002` → `VCG-B-05` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as the inner reception and grasp of revealed truth — the capacity to perceive insight into mystery, to receive what God gives, and to resist what God thwarts
- **NEW** (God's perceptive comprehension of the human person: bin / bi.nah as divine knowing): God's inner perceptive faculty directed toward the human person — his understanding of thoughts, deeds, plans, and the heart. Divine understanding of the human is comprehensive and intimate.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 24:12 (H0995)

##### `816-002` → `VCG-B-15` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names understanding as the inner reception and grasp of revealed truth — the capacity to perceive insight into mystery, to receive what God gives, and to resist what God thwarts
- **NEW** (suniēmi / sunesis: inner comprehension of mystery as divine gift): The inner comprehension of what was hidden — the mystery of Christ, the mystery of God's will — given as a divine endowment, not acquired by human intelligence.
- _Sample verse:_ 2Ti 2:7 (G4907)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-A-01` (1 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (Wisdom as constituted inner quality of character: cha.kham as holistic inner endowment): Wisdom as a defining inner quality of the person — not a skill or technique but a whole-person orientation that shows in perception, speech, conduct, and relationships. The quality is positive and characterises those who are genuinely wise.
- _Sample verse:_ Hos 14:9 (H0995)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-A-08` (1 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (Craft skill applied to secular or non-sacred purposes: cha.kham and cha.shav in craft outside the sanctuary): The same inner capacity for craft skill and design applied outside the sacred context — to ships, idols, military machines, and instruments of music.
- _Sample verse:_ Jer 9:17 (H0995)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-B-10` (1 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (Limits of human understanding before divine mystery: bin / bi.nah facing what cannot be grasped): The person exercises the inner perceptive faculty but reaches its boundary — divine works, cosmic scale, the mystery of God's ways are simply beyond human comprehension.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 20:24 (H0995)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-C-03` (1 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (da.at as instrument of divine work and Spirit-endowment): Knowledge as a Spirit-given capacity; as a divine attribute; as the instrument of the Servant's justifying work. These are cases where da.at has extraordinary theological weight.
- _Sample verse:_ Dan 1:4 (H0995)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-C-10` (1 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (ya.da as moral knowledge guiding right action): The inner moral knowing that directs the righteous person — knowing what is acceptable, what is just, what is right. Its absence names moral blindness; its presence names moral clarity.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 28:5 (H0995)

##### `932-001` → `VCG-E-01` (1 verses)

- **DB**: bin as the inner perceptive faculty in its constituted form — the quality of the wise, discerning person. The faculty is seated in the heart (1Ki 3:9, Psa 49:20), enables right judgment (1Ki 3:9,11), receives instruction (Pro 9:8), perceives situations rightly (2Sa 12:19, Job 6:30), and is the inner capacity from which wise conduct flows. It is morally conditioned — it enables covenant-keeping (Deu 4:6) and is blocked by the absence of the fear of the Lord.
- **NEW** (Human counsel: wisdom given between persons shaping deliberation): One person gives advice or counsel to another — the inner wisdom of the advisor expressed and offered to shape the recipient's purposes. The outcome depends on whether counsel is received or rejected.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 3:3 (H0995)

##### `932-002` → `VCG-A-12` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the prayerful seeking and receiving of understanding from God — the inner posture of humility and petition before God for discernment
- **NEW** (se.khel: discernment as personal inner quality producing good outcomes): A distinctive inner quality of practical wisdom — discernment, good sense, shrewd perception — that produces favourable outcomes and is recognisable in persons.
- _Sample verse:_ Neh 8:8 (H0995)

##### `932-002` → `VCG-B-11` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the prayerful seeking and receiving of understanding from God — the inner posture of humility and petition before God for discernment
- **NEW** (Directional attending: bin as perceptive attention directed toward an object): Bin used in the sense of directing perceptive attention toward something — looking closely, examining carefully, paying attention. Distinct from understanding as comprehension. The faculty is directed attention, not cognitive grasping.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 32:7 (H0995)

##### `932-002` → `VCG-C-07` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the prayerful seeking and receiving of understanding from God — the inner posture of humility and petition before God for discernment
- **NEW** (ya.da as the "then you shall know" pattern: divine self-disclosure through event producing recognition): A repeated pattern across the OT: God acts, and the purpose of the action is that persons will know — know that he is the Lord, that he is present, that he sent his messenger. The knowing is produced by the event, not by the seeker.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 43:10 (H0995)

##### `932-002` → `VCG-C-12` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the prayerful seeking and receiving of understanding from God — the inner posture of humility and petition before God for discernment
- **NEW** (ya.da as limits of human knowing before divine mystery): Human ya.da encountering its own limits before God's work, purposes, and nature — cannot comprehend, cannot find, cannot know the end or the route.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 40:21 (H0995)

##### `932-002` → `VCG-F-02` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the prayerful seeking and receiving of understanding from God — the inner posture of humility and petition before God for discernment
- **NEW** (Meditative dwelling on God's law, precepts, and word: si.ach as law-meditation): The sustained inward dwelling on God's law, precepts, statutes, and promises — the defining meditative practice of the devoted person. The object is always divine instruction. All uses from Psalm 119.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 119:27 (H0995)

##### `932-003` → `VCG-B-04` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names God's inner comprehension of the human person — God's perception, understanding, and attending to the heart, thought, and deed
- **NEW** (Understanding gained through seeking and engagement with the word and covenant): Understanding as the fruit of deliberate orientation toward God — seeking, keeping the precepts, holding to the covenant. The faculty grows and deepens through the person's active engagement.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 28:23 (H0995)

##### `932-003` → `VCG-B-11` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names God's inner comprehension of the human person — God's perception, understanding, and attending to the heart, thought, and deed
- **NEW** (Directional attending: bin as perceptive attention directed toward an object): Bin used in the sense of directing perceptive attention toward something — looking closely, examining carefully, paying attention. Distinct from understanding as comprehension. The faculty is directed attention, not cognitive grasping.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 30:20 (H0995)

##### `932-004` → `VCG-B-08` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the failure, hardening, or absence of inner understanding — spiritual blindness, incapacity to perceive God or moral reality, and the rhetorical limits of human comprehension before God
- **NEW** (Christ opening minds to understand: suniēmi as receptive inner comprehension activated): The positive activation of the inner perceptive faculty — Christ opening minds, understanding breaking through, the disciples receiving what had previously been closed to them.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 15:10 (G4920)

##### `932-004` → `VCG-C-13` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the failure, hardening, or absence of inner understanding — spiritual blindness, incapacity to perceive God or moral reality, and the rhetorical limits of human comprehension before God
- **NEW** (de.ah as the knowledge of the Lord filling the earth: eschatological covenantal knowing): Knowledge of the Lord as the content of the eschatological promise — universal, filling, covering as the waters cover the sea.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 28:9 (H0995)

##### `932-004` → `VCG-D-03` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the failure, hardening, or absence of inner understanding — spiritual blindness, incapacity to perceive God or moral reality, and the rhetorical limits of human comprehension before God
- **NEW** (Evaluative regard of persons and things: assigning worth or category by reckoning): One person (human or divine) evaluates another person, group, or thing by reckoning — assigning them a worth, category, or status. The reckoning is relational and evaluative, not judicial-moral as in VCG-D-01. Includes both positive and negative assessments, and both legitimate and contested evaluations.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 29:16 (H0995)

---

### M15-C

_602 rows_

#### a. New VCGs derived (from v2)

| Code | Title | Verses |
|---|---|---:|
| `VCG-A-01` | Wisdom as constituted inner quality of character: cha.kham as holistic inner endowment | 6 |
| `VCG-A-02` | Wisdom as governance qualification: cha.kham as inner capacity required for leadership | 3 |
| `VCG-A-03` | Professional court wise men as institutional class: cha.kham / chak.kim as class title | 1 |
| `VCG-A-11` | tu.shiy.yah: sound wisdom as effective inner resource | 2 |
| `VCG-B-01` | bin / bi.nah as constituted inner perceptive faculty: understanding governing speech, relationships, and perception | 2 |
| `VCG-B-03` | Spirit-given understanding: bin / bi.nah / te.vu.nah as a divine endowment | 3 |
| `VCG-B-04` | Understanding gained through seeking and engagement with the word and covenant | 3 |
| `VCG-B-05` | God's perceptive comprehension of the human person: bin / bi.nah as divine knowing | 2 |
| `VCG-B-06` | Failed or absent understanding: bin as the person who cannot perceive | 2 |
| `VCG-B-07` | Judicial withholding of understanding: suniēmi / bin as blocked comprehension | 1 |
| `VCG-B-10` | Limits of human understanding before divine mystery: bin / bi.nah facing what cannot be grasped | 3 |
| `VCG-C-01` | da.at as inner possession: knowledge as an inner quality of the wise person | 49 |
| `VCG-C-02` | da.at of God: the knowledge of God as the defining inner orientation of the covenantal person | 9 |
| `VCG-C-03` | da.at as instrument of divine work and Spirit-endowment | 7 |
| `VCG-C-04` | da.at as absent in the foolish and hollow | 8 |
| `VCG-C-05` | da.at as inner intent determining moral status of an act | 4 |
| `VCG-C-06` | ya.da as covenantal knowing between God and Israel: relational election knowing | 37 |
| `VCG-C-07` | ya.da as the "then you shall know" pattern: divine self-disclosure through event producing recognition | 19 |
| `VCG-C-08` | ya.da as God's comprehensive knowing of persons: divine inner knowledge of the human | 20 |
| `VCG-C-09` | ya.da as self-knowledge: the person's inner knowledge of their own condition | 15 |
| `VCG-C-10` | ya.da as moral knowledge guiding right action | 14 |
| `VCG-C-11` | ya.da as Israel's failure to know God: broken or absent covenantal knowing | 2 |
| `VCG-C-12` | ya.da as limits of human knowing before divine mystery | 12 |
| `VCG-C-13` | de.ah as the knowledge of the Lord filling the earth: eschatological covenantal knowing | 7 |
| `VCG-C-14` | de.a as formed inner opinion or divine perfect knowing | 6 |
| `VCG-C-15` | man.da as reason: the defining inner seat of humanness | 4 |
| `VCG-C-16` | oida as settled inner conviction shaping conduct and orientation | 17 |
| `VCG-C-17` | oida as identity-shaping knowledge: knowing who you are in Christ | 8 |
| `VCG-C-19` | oida as knowledge divorced from love: the hollow inner capacity | 2 |
| `VCG-C-20` | agnoeō: culpable spiritual ignorance of God's ways and character | 7 |
| `VCG-D-03` | Evaluative regard of persons and things: assigning worth or category by reckoning | 1 |
| `VCG-D-05` | sa.khal as perceptive prudent discernment: seeing clearly what is before you | 2 |
| `VCG-D-06` | a.rum / a.rom: prudent inner disposition as perceptive self-governance | 1 |
| `VCG-E-04` | Divine counsel: God's sovereign purposive intent directed toward nations and history | 1 |
| `VCG-E-14` | Purposive inner intention set before the will: protithēmi as planned goal | 1 |
| `VCG-E-16` | The rational explanatory faculty: chesh.bon seeking the scheme of things | 1 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-A-01** — _Wisdom as a defining inner quality of the person — not a skill or technique but a whole-person orientation that shows in perception, speech, conduct, and relationships. The quality is positive and characterises those who are genuinely wise._
- **VCG-A-02** — _Wisdom as the specific qualification needed for the exercise of leadership and governance — it is the inner quality that enables just rule, right appointments, and effective governance._
- **VCG-A-03** — _The court class of professional wise men — summoned for interpretation, giving counsel, named as the foil for what Spirit-given wisdom can do. Their title and incapacity stand together in the Daniel narratives._
- **VCG-A-11** — _Sound wisdom as a substantial, effective inner capacity — held by God, available to the upright, able to sustain and protect, violated by isolation, equated with the fear of God._
- **VCG-B-01** — _Understanding as a substantive inner quality of the person — what they are characterised by. The faculty is active, receptive, and productive: it governs what the wise person perceives, how they speak, and how they relate. The person of understanding is defined by this quality._
- **VCG-B-03** — _Understanding as explicitly God-given — the inner capacity placed within the person by God or the Spirit, not acquired through human effort. Includes craft intelligence for sacred work and the Messiah's Spirit-given understanding._
- **VCG-B-04** — _Understanding as the fruit of deliberate orientation toward God — seeking, keeping the precepts, holding to the covenant. The faculty grows and deepens through the person's active engagement._
- **VCG-B-05** — _God's inner perceptive faculty directed toward the human person — his understanding of thoughts, deeds, plans, and the heart. Divine understanding of the human is comprehensive and intimate._
- **VCG-B-06** — _Understanding absent in persons or groups — whether through their own failure, the consequence of wickedness, the absence of the divine gift, or Israel's characteristic blindness._
- **VCG-B-07** — _Understanding deliberately withheld by God — the inner faculty is present but its activation is prevented by divine judgment. Hearing without receiving; perception without comprehension._
- **VCG-B-10** — _The person exercises the inner perceptive faculty but reaches its boundary — divine works, cosmic scale, the mystery of God's ways are simply beyond human comprehension._
- **VCG-C-01** — _Knowledge as what the wise person holds inwardly — the inner capacity/content that Proverbs aims to produce, that the wise accumulate and guard, and that gives the person strength._
- **VCG-C-02** — _Knowledge of God as the substance of the inner life — what it is to know God relationally and ethically. Includes both positive possession and its absence._
- **VCG-C-03** — _Knowledge as a Spirit-given capacity; as a divine attribute; as the instrument of the Servant's justifying work. These are cases where da.at has extraordinary theological weight._
- **VCG-C-04** — _Knowledge as what is absent, empty, or distorted — speech without knowledge; wisdom that has become falsehood._
- **VCG-C-05** — _Da.at (or its absence) as what determines whether an act is intentional — presence of da.at/knowing means wilful; absence means unintentional. The inner moral condition determines culpability._
- **VCG-C-06** — _The most intimate form of ya.da — God's elective knowing of Israel and Israel's knowing of God as the substance of the covenant relationship. Not merely informational but constitutively relational and moral._
- **VCG-C-07** — _A repeated pattern across the OT: God acts, and the purpose of the action is that persons will know — know that he is the Lord, that he is present, that he sent his messenger. The knowing is produced by the event, not by the seeker._
- **VCG-C-08** — _God's knowing of the person's inner life — motives, character, acts, plans, future tendencies. Comprehensive, attentive, penetrating._
- **VCG-C-09** — _The person's inner knowing of their own moral state, situation, character, or experience. Includes both honest and distorted self-knowledge._
- **VCG-C-10** — _The inner moral knowing that directs the righteous person — knowing what is acceptable, what is just, what is right. Its absence names moral blindness; its presence names moral clarity._
- **VCG-C-11** — _Israel's characteristic failure to know God — receiving his gifts without recognising the giver; claiming to know while pursuing other gods; the people who do not perceive._
- **VCG-C-12** — _Human ya.da encountering its own limits before God's work, purposes, and nature — cannot comprehend, cannot find, cannot know the end or the route._
- **VCG-C-13** — _Knowledge of the Lord as the content of the eschatological promise — universal, filling, covering as the waters cover the sea._
- **VCG-C-14** — _Elihu's inner formed judgment held inwardly and now to be expressed; or applied to God's perfect knowledge of his own works._
- **VCG-C-15** — _Man.da names reason as the inner capacity whose loss reduces the person to the level of animals and whose restoration constitutes restored human dignity._
- **VCG-C-16** — _The NT knowing that is not primarily relational or covenantal but convictional — settled inner knowledge about theological facts, moral patterns, and eschatological realities that should orient conduct._
- **VCG-C-17** — _The "do you not know" pattern — Paul's repeated challenge to a community that possesses this knowledge but does not act from it. The knowing shapes identity and therefore conduct._
- **VCG-C-19** — _Knowledge that exists without love is named explicitly as capable of being emptied of worth — inflating rather than building._
- **VCG-C-20** — _The inner condition of not knowing God's ways, righteousness, or purposes — when the ignorance is morally significant, not merely informational._
- **VCG-D-03** — _One person (human or divine) evaluates another person, group, or thing by reckoning — assigning them a worth, category, or status. The reckoning is relational and evaluative, not judicial-moral as in VCG-D-01. Includes both positive and negative assessments, and both legitimate and contested evaluations._
- **VCG-D-05** — _The inner capacity for perceptive attending — seeing God's acts, situations, or conditions with clarity and wisdom. The prudent person considers, ponders, observes rightly where others miss or fail to attend._
- **VCG-D-06** — _The inner quality of prudence in the sense of perceptive self-governance — seeing situations clearly and governing speech and conduct with care. Directionally neutral: serves righteousness (Proverbs uses) or deception (Gen 3:1, Job 15:5)._
- **VCG-E-04** — _God forms and executes sovereign intention that cannot be annulled or redirected. His counsel is self-originating, irresistible, and encompasses the whole of history. Multiple human terms (ya.ats, cha.shav, za.mam) converge in expressing this._
- **VCG-E-14** — _The act of setting a goal or purpose before the will — either human (a travel intention repeatedly frustrated) or divine (God setting forth Christ as propitiation from an eternal purpose)._
- **VCG-E-16** — _The inner capacity for rational explanation and calculation — the mind seeking to understand the underlying structure of reality. Belongs to the living; ceases at death._
