#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `955-001` → `VCG-C-01` (43 verses)

- **DB**: Knowledge as the foundational inner capacity — rooted in the fear of the Lord (Pro 1:7) and experienced inwardly as delight in the soul (Pro 2:10); the cognitive-spiritual capacity that grounds wisdom.
- **NEW** (da.at as inner possession: knowledge as an inner quality of the wise person): Knowledge as what the wise person holds inwardly — the inner capacity/content that Proverbs aims to produce, that the wise accumulate and guard, and that gives the person strength.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 13:2 (H1847)

##### `958-001` → `VCG-C-06` (36 verses)

- **DB**: Covenantal/relational knowing between God and Israel
- **NEW** (ya.da as covenantal knowing between God and Israel: relational election knowing): The most intimate form of ya.da — God's elective knowing of Israel and Israel's knowing of God as the substance of the covenant relationship. Not merely informational but constitutively relational and moral.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 18:19 (H3045)

##### `963-001` → `VCG-C-16` (17 verses)

- **DB**: Settled inner conviction orienting moral, spiritual, and relational life toward God
- **NEW** (oida as settled inner conviction shaping conduct and orientation): The NT knowing that is not primarily relational or covenantal but convictional — settled inner knowledge about theological facts, moral patterns, and eschatological realities that should orient conduct.
- _Sample verse:_ Rom 2:2 (G6063)

##### `958-003` → `VCG-C-08` (16 verses)

- **DB**: God's comprehensive knowledge of the inner person — motives, character, inner states
- **NEW** (ya.da as God's comprehensive knowing of persons: divine inner knowledge of the human): God's knowing of the person's inner life — motives, character, acts, plans, future tendencies. Comprehensive, attentive, penetrating.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 18:21 (H3045)

##### `958-001` → `VCG-C-07` (14 verses)

- **DB**: Covenantal/relational knowing between God and Israel
- **NEW** (ya.da as the "then you shall know" pattern: divine self-disclosure through event producing recognition): A repeated pattern across the OT: God acts, and the purpose of the action is that persons will know — know that he is the Lord, that he is present, that he sent his messenger. The knowing is produced by the event, not by the seeker.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 29:6 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-C-10` (13 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (ya.da as moral knowledge guiding right action): The inner moral knowing that directs the righteous person — knowing what is acceptable, what is just, what is right. Its absence names moral blindness; its presence names moral clarity.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 3:22 (H3045)

##### `958-002` → `VCG-C-09` (10 verses)

- **DB**: Self-knowledge of inner moral condition, guilt, capacity before God
- **NEW** (ya.da as self-knowledge: the person's inner knowledge of their own condition): The person's inner knowing of their own moral state, situation, character, or experience. Includes both honest and distorted self-knowledge.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 4:9 (H3045)

##### `955-005` → `VCG-C-04` (8 verses)

- **DB**: Limits and failures of human knowledge as inner condition producing ruin
- **NEW** (da.at as absent in the foolish and hollow): Knowledge as what is absent, empty, or distorted — speech without knowledge; wisdom that has become falsehood.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 15:2 (H1847)

##### `958-002` → `VCG-C-12` (8 verses)

- **DB**: Self-knowledge of inner moral condition, guilt, capacity before God
- **NEW** (ya.da as limits of human knowing before divine mystery): Human ya.da encountering its own limits before God's work, purposes, and nature — cannot comprehend, cannot find, cannot know the end or the route.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 8:9 (H3045)

##### `963-003` → `VCG-C-17` (8 verses)

- **DB**: Identity-shaping knowledge — who the person is in Christ, transforming inner orientation
- **NEW** (oida as identity-shaping knowledge: knowing who you are in Christ): The "do you not know" pattern — Paul's repeated challenge to a community that possesses this knowledge but does not act from it. The knowing shapes identity and therefore conduct.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 3:16 (G6063)

##### `1838-001` → `VCG-C-20` (7 verses)

- **DB**: Term names culpable spiritual ignorance — the inner condition of not knowing God's character, ways, or will, which becomes the basis of moral failure or self-deception
- **NEW** (agnoeō: culpable spiritual ignorance of God's ways and character): The inner condition of not knowing God's ways, righteousness, or purposes — when the ignorance is morally significant, not merely informational.
- _Sample verse:_ Act 13:27 (G0050)

##### `955-002` → `VCG-C-02` (7 verses)

- **DB**: Knowledge of God as defining inner orientation — presence = faithfulness, absence = ruin
- **NEW** (da.at of God: the knowledge of God as the defining inner orientation of the covenantal person): Knowledge of God as the substance of the inner life — what it is to know God relationally and ethically. Includes both positive possession and its absence.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 21:14 (H1847)

##### `955-003` → `VCG-C-03` (6 verses)

- **DB**: Knowledge as Spirit-given inner endowment — bestowed from above
- **NEW** (da.at as instrument of divine work and Spirit-endowment): Knowledge as a Spirit-given capacity; as a divine attribute; as the instrument of the Servant's justifying work. These are cases where da.at has extraordinary theological weight.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 21:22 (H1847)

##### `958-005` → `VCG-C-07` (5 verses)

- **DB**: God's revelatory self-disclosure — his acts, name, and purposes made known that the human person may come to recognise, receive, and respond inwardly to God's sovereign purposes.
- **NEW** (ya.da as the "then you shall know" pattern: divine self-disclosure through event producing recognition): A repeated pattern across the OT: God acts, and the purpose of the action is that persons will know — know that he is the Lord, that he is present, that he sent his messenger. The knowing is produced by the event, not by the seeker.
- _Sample verse:_ Jos 3:7 (H3045)

##### `955-004` → `VCG-C-05` (4 verses)

- **DB**: Moral condition of inner intent — presence or absence determining accountability
- **NEW** (da.at as inner intent determining moral status of an act): Da.at (or its absence) as what determines whether an act is intentional — presence of da.at/knowing means wilful; absence means unintentional. The inner moral condition determines culpability.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 4:42 (H1847)

##### `963-002` → `VCG-C-09` (4 verses)

- **DB**: Self-knowledge of inner conflict — awareness of flesh, sin, and spiritual limitation
- **NEW** (ya.da as self-knowledge: the person's inner knowledge of their own condition): The person's inner knowing of their own moral state, situation, character, or experience. Includes both honest and distorted self-knowledge.
- _Sample verse:_ Rom 7:18 (G6063)

##### `(none)` → `VCG-A-01` (3 verses)

- **DB**: _(no DB description)_
- **NEW** (Wisdom as constituted inner quality of character: cha.kham as holistic inner endowment): Wisdom as a defining inner quality of the person — not a skill or technique but a whole-person orientation that shows in perception, speech, conduct, and relationships. The quality is positive and characterises those who are genuinely wise.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 9:9 (H3045)

##### `(none)` → `VCG-A-02` (3 verses)

- **DB**: _(no DB description)_
- **NEW** (Wisdom as governance qualification: cha.kham as inner capacity required for leadership): Wisdom as the specific qualification needed for the exercise of leadership and governance — it is the inner quality that enables just rule, right appointments, and effective governance.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 1:13 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-A-01` (3 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (Wisdom as constituted inner quality of character: cha.kham as holistic inner endowment): Wisdom as a defining inner quality of the person — not a skill or technique but a whole-person orientation that shows in perception, speech, conduct, and relationships. The quality is positive and characterises those who are genuinely wise.
- _Sample verse:_ Ecc 8:1 (H3045)

##### `959-001` → `VCG-C-13` (3 verses)

- **DB**: God's perfect knowledge as the ground of moral accountability — all human action weighed by him (1Sa 2:3); and the inner rebellion of those who deny God's knowledge (Psa 73:11), refusing moral scrutiny.
- **NEW** (de.ah as the knowledge of the Lord filling the earth: eschatological covenantal knowing): Knowledge of the Lord as the content of the eschatological promise — universal, filling, covering as the waters cover the sea.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Sa 2:3 (H1844)

##### `959-002` → `VCG-C-13` (3 verses)

- **DB**: Knowledge of God as content of inner formation — taught, sought, filling the person
- **NEW** (de.ah as the knowledge of the Lord filling the earth: eschatological covenantal knowing): Knowledge of the Lord as the content of the eschatological promise — universal, filling, covering as the waters cover the sea.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 11:9 (H1844)

##### `961-001` → `VCG-C-14` (3 verses)

- **DB**: Inner formed judgment or opinion held and expressed or withheld
- **NEW** (de.a as formed inner opinion or divine perfect knowing): Elihu's inner formed judgment held inwardly and now to be expressed; or applied to God's perfect knowledge of his own works.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 32:6 (H1843)

##### `963-004` → `VCG-C-08` (3 verses)

- **DB**: God's or another's knowledge of the inner person — hearts, thoughts, sincerity
- **NEW** (ya.da as God's comprehensive knowing of persons: divine inner knowledge of the human): God's knowing of the person's inner life — motives, character, acts, plans, future tendencies. Comprehensive, attentive, penetrating.

##### `(none)` → `VCG-B-10` (2 verses)

##### `958-001` → `VCG-C-11` (2 verses)

##### `958-003` → `VCG-B-04` (1 verses)

- **DB**: God's comprehensive knowledge of the inner person — motives, character, inner states
- **NEW** (Understanding gained through seeking and engagement with the word and covenant): Understanding as the fruit of deliberate orientation toward God — seeking, keeping the precepts, holding to the covenant. The faculty grows and deepens through the person's active engagement.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 28:23 (H3045)

##### `958-003` → `VCG-C-06` (1 verses)

- **DB**: God's comprehensive knowledge of the inner person — motives, character, inner states
- **NEW** (ya.da as covenantal knowing between God and Israel: relational election knowing): The most intimate form of ya.da — God's elective knowing of Israel and Israel's knowing of God as the substance of the covenant relationship. Not merely informational but constitutively relational and moral.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Sa 3:13 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-A-03` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (Professional court wise men as institutional class: cha.kham / chak.kim as class title): The court class of professional wise men — summoned for interpretation, giving counsel, named as the foil for what Spirit-given wisdom can do. Their title and incapacity stand together in the Daniel narratives.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 34:2 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-B-01` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (bin / bi.nah as constituted inner perceptive faculty: understanding governing speech, relationships, and perception): Understanding as a substantive inner quality of the person — what they are characterised by. The faculty is active, receptive, and productive: it governs what the wise person perceives, how they speak, and how they relate. The person of understanding is defined by this quality.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 28:2 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-B-06` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (Failed or absent understanding: bin as the person who cannot perceive): Understanding absent in persons or groups — whether through their own failure, the consequence of wickedness, the absence of the divine gift, or Israel's characteristic blindness.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 56:11 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-B-07` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (Judicial withholding of understanding: suniēmi / bin as blocked comprehension): Understanding deliberately withheld by God — the inner faculty is present but its activation is prevented by divine judgment. Hearing without receiving; perception without comprehension.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 6:9 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-C-01` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (da.at as inner possession: knowledge as an inner quality of the wise person): Knowledge as what the wise person holds inwardly — the inner capacity/content that Proverbs aims to produce, that the wise accumulate and guard, and that gives the person strength.
- _Sample verse:_ Pro 29:7 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-C-09` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (ya.da as self-knowledge: the person's inner knowledge of their own condition): The person's inner knowing of their own moral state, situation, character, or experience. Includes both honest and distorted self-knowledge.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 3:7 (H3045)

##### `958-004` → `VCG-D-05` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Moral knowledge guiding right action — knowing good, evil, justice
- **NEW** (sa.khal as perceptive prudent discernment: seeing clearly what is before you): The inner capacity for perceptive attending — seeing God's acts, situations, or conditions with clarity and wisdom. The prudent person considers, ponders, observes rightly where others miss or fail to attend.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 44:18 (H3045)

##### `958-005` → `VCG-C-12` (1 verses)

- **DB**: God's revelatory self-disclosure — his acts, name, and purposes made known that the human person may come to recognise, receive, and respond inwardly to God's sovereign purposes.
- **NEW** (ya.da as limits of human knowing before divine mystery): Human ya.da encountering its own limits before God's work, purposes, and nature — cannot comprehend, cannot find, cannot know the end or the route.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 40:21 (H3045)

---

### M15-D

_168 rows_

#### a. New VCGs derived (from v2)

| Code | Title | Verses |
|---|---|---:|
| `VCG-A-11` | tu.shiy.yah: sound wisdom as effective inner resource | 1 |
| `VCG-D-01` | Divine moral imputation: crediting or not-crediting righteousness/guilt before God | 6 |
| `VCG-D-02` | Inner self-examination: deliberate attending to one's own ways, forming a judgment | 11 |
| `VCG-D-03` | Evaluative regard of persons and things: assigning worth or category by reckoning | 31 |
| `VCG-D-04` | sa.khal as prudent wisdom-in-action: conduct aligned with God's ways producing success | 8 |
| `VCG-D-05` | sa.khal as perceptive prudent discernment: seeing clearly what is before you | 41 |
| `VCG-D-06` | a.rum / a.rom: prudent inner disposition as perceptive self-governance | 12 |
| `VCG-D-07` | ta.am: taste as the faculty of inner discernment | 7 |
| `VCG-D-08` | diakrinō as discriminating judgment: inner act of making evaluative distinctions between persons or matters | 10 |
| `VCG-D-09` | diakrinō as inner self-division: the heart split between faith and hesitation | 6 |
| `VCG-D-10` | logismos: inner arguments and conflicting thoughts as the site of conscience and spiritual contest | 2 |
| `VCG-D-11` | aisthētērion: the cultivated inner faculty of moral discernment | 1 |
| `VCG-E-02` | Hostile human counsel: devising harm through purposive inner planning against another | 1 |
| `VCG-F-03` | All-day sustained meditation as the ground of understanding: si.chah | 1 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-A-11** — _Sound wisdom as a substantial, effective inner capacity — held by God, available to the upright, able to sustain and protect, violated by isolation, equated with the fear of God._
- **VCG-D-01** — _The inner divine act of reckoning a moral status to a person — positive (faith counted as righteousness; act counted as righteousness) or negative (bloodguilt imputed; iniquity not counted). The reckoning is judicial and moral, not merely classificatory. The subject is always God or divine authority._
- **VCG-D-02** — _The person turns attention inwardly and forms an assessment of their own conduct, situation, or moral standing — not reckoning another, but deliberating about oneself or one's circumstances._
- **VCG-D-03** — _One person (human or divine) evaluates another person, group, or thing by reckoning — assigning them a worth, category, or status. The reckoning is relational and evaluative, not judicial-moral as in VCG-D-01. Includes both positive and negative assessments, and both legitimate and contested evaluations._
- **VCG-D-04** — _The inner quality of prudence expressed in action that is aligned with God's instruction, covenant, or character. The action is both wise (correctly oriented) and effective (produces prospered outcomes). Wisdom and success are co-present._
- **VCG-D-05** — _The inner capacity for perceptive attending — seeing God's acts, situations, or conditions with clarity and wisdom. The prudent person considers, ponders, observes rightly where others miss or fail to attend._
- **VCG-D-06** — _The inner quality of prudence in the sense of perceptive self-governance — seeing situations clearly and governing speech and conduct with care. Directionally neutral: serves righteousness (Proverbs uses) or deception (Gen 3:1, Job 15:5)._
- **VCG-D-07** — _The palate's capacity to test and evaluate food serves as the image for the inner faculty of discerning and testing. Used directly of food-tasting and figuratively of testing words, situations, and the goodness of God._
- **VCG-D-08** — _The inner act of judging and distinguishing — discerning between persons, weighing speech, making or not-making discriminations. The judgment can be right (weighing prophecy, discerning the Lord's body) or wrong (partiality, unjust criticism)._
- **VCG-D-09** — _The person's inner life is not unified — faith and doubt or hesitation coexist, producing wavering, instability, and inability to act from whole-hearted trust._
- **VCG-D-10** — _The inner cognitive conflict — thoughts that accuse or excuse (conscience), and arguments or reasoning structures raised against God that must be brought into captivity. Both uses name the inner cognitive life as a contested site._
- **VCG-D-11** — _Single verse. Names moral discernment as a trainable inner faculty — not innate but developed through practice. The mature person's ability to distinguish good from evil is an acquired capacity._
- **VCG-E-02** — _The inner forming of purposive schemes or counsel directed toward harming another person or group. The devising is deliberate, premeditated, and inner — formed in the heart before being enacted._
- **VCG-F-03** — _Sustained, all-day meditative engagement with God's testimonies as the practice that produces understanding — more than teachers can give._

#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `519-001` → `VCG-D-05` (41 verses)

- **DB**: Term names prudent wisdom as an inner capacity — understanding, considering, and perceiving wisely as an orientation toward God and truth
- **NEW** (sa.khal as perceptive prudent discernment: seeing clearly what is before you): The inner capacity for perceptive attending — seeing God's acts, situations, or conditions with clarity and wisdom. The prudent person considers, ponders, observes rightly where others miss or fail to attend.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 32:29 (H7919A)

##### `3335-002` → `VCG-D-03` (15 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the evaluative regard of persons or things — the inner act of assessing worth, status, or character in relational and social contexts
- **NEW** (Evaluative regard of persons and things: assigning worth or category by reckoning): One person (human or divine) evaluates another person, group, or thing by reckoning — assigning them a worth, category, or status. The reckoning is relational and evaluative, not judicial-moral as in VCG-D-01. Includes both positive and negative assessments, and both legitimate and contested evaluations.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 31:15 (H2803H)

##### `3336-002` → `VCG-D-03` (15 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner evaluative act of counting or regarding — assessing a person's or thing's worth, status, or standing
- **NEW** (Evaluative regard of persons and things: assigning worth or category by reckoning): One person (human or divine) evaluates another person, group, or thing by reckoning — assigning them a worth, category, or status. The reckoning is relational and evaluative, not judicial-moral as in VCG-D-01. Includes both positive and negative assessments, and both legitimate and contested evaluations.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 2:11 (H2803J)

##### `3336-001` → `VCG-D-02` (11 verses)

- **NEW** (Inner self-examination: deliberate attending to one's own ways, forming a judgment): The person turns attention inwardly and forms an assessment of their own conduct, situation, or moral standing — not reckoning another, but deliberating about oneself or one's circumstances.

The judgment can be right (weighing prophecy, discerning the Lord's body) or wrong (partiality, unjust criticism).

- **NEW** (sa.khal as prudent wisdom-in-action: conduct aligned with God's ways producing success): The inner quality of prudence expressed in action that is aligned with God's instruction, covenant, or character. The action is both wise (correctly oriented) and effective (produces prospered outcomes). Wisdom and success are co-present.

##### `3335-001` → `VCG-D-01` (6 verses)

##### `5099-002` → `VCG-D-03` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the abstaining from taste as an expression of inner grief or penitence — the voluntary refusal to eat as the outward form of an inward state of mourning or contrition
- **NEW** (Evaluative regard of persons and things: assigning worth or category by reckoning): One person (human or divine) evaluates another person, group, or thing by reckoning — assigning them a worth, category, or status. The reckoning is relational and evaluative, not judicial-moral as in VCG-D-01. Includes both positive and negative assessments, and both legitimate and contested evaluations.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 53:3 (H2803H)

##### `519-001` → `VCG-D-04` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names prudent wisdom as an inner capacity — understanding, considering, and perceiving wisely as an orientation toward God and truth
- **NEW** (sa.khal as prudent wisdom-in-action: conduct aligned with God's ways producing success): The inner quality of prudence expressed in action that is aligned with God's instruction, covenant, or character. The action is both wise (correctly oriented) and effective (produces prospered outcomes). Wisdom and success are co-present.
- _Sample verse:_ Deu 29:9 (H7919A)

##### `519-001` → `VCG-F-03` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names prudent wisdom as an inner capacity — understanding, considering, and perceiving wisely as an orientation toward God and truth
- **NEW** (All-day sustained meditation as the ground of understanding: si.chah): Sustained, all-day meditative engagement with God's testimonies as the practice that produces understanding — more than teachers can give.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 119:99 (H7919A)

##### `818-001` → `VCG-D-11` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner faculty of moral discernment — the trained and exercised capacity to distinguish good from evil; discernment as a developed inner capability
- **NEW** (aisthētērion: the cultivated inner faculty of moral discernment): Single verse. Names moral discernment as a trainable inner faculty — not innate but developed through practice. The mature person's ability to distinguish good from evil is an acquired capacity.
- _Sample verse:_ Heb 5:14 (G0145)

### M15-E

_190 rows_

#### a. New VCGs derived (from v2)

| Code | Title | Verses |
|---|---|---:|
| `VCG-E-01` | Human counsel: wisdom given between persons shaping deliberation | 33 |
| `VCG-E-02` | Hostile human counsel: devising harm through purposive inner planning against another | 27 |
| `VCG-E-03` | Noble inner purposing: counsel as expression of moral character | 4 |
| `VCG-E-04` | Divine counsel: God's sovereign purposive intent directed toward nations and history | 16 |
| `VCG-E-05` | Divine purposive planning with conditional openness to relenting | 7 |
| `VCG-E-06` | Purposive divine and human intent working through the same event toward opposite ends | 1 |
| `VCG-E-07` | God's purposive care for the individual: divine inner attending and planning for the needy | 4 |
| `VCG-E-08` | God's purposive planning for his people's welfare: the plans-for-welfare pattern | 1 |
| `VCG-E-09` | Human volitional intent: boulomai naming purposive inner will in motion | 21 |
| `VCG-E-10` | God's sovereign purposive will: boulomai naming divine willing in disclosure, creation, and redemption | 6 |
| `VCG-E-11` | Deliberate inner decision-making: bouleuō as the mind resolving upon a course of action | 4 |
| `VCG-E-12` | Deliberate resolve to harm: bouleuō naming purposive decision directed against another | 3 |
| `VCG-E-13` | Considered personal judgment: gnōmē as authoritative inner resolution | 7 |
| `VCG-E-14` | Purposive inner intention set before the will: protithēmi as planned goal | 3 |
| `VCG-E-15` | Purposeful foresight and provision: pronoia as governance foresight or deliberate inner provision | 2 |
| `VCG-E-16` | The rational explanatory faculty: chesh.bon seeking the scheme of things | 3 |
| `VCG-E-17` | Royal inner decisional planning: a.shit naming a king's purposive appointment | 1 |
| `VCG-E-18` | The appeal for divine purposive attending: a.shat as hope for divine attention in crisis | 1 |
| `VCG-E-19` | Active deliberate inner attending: shit as sustained purposive attention | 4 |
| `VCG-E-20` | Failure or suppression of inner attending: shit as non-engagement | 3 |
| `VCG-E-21` | Communal deliberate purposing: uts as collective counsel-forming | 2 |
| `VCG-E-22` | Human purposeful resolve: za.mam as intent formed and set out to achieve | 1 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-E-01** — _One person gives advice or counsel to another — the inner wisdom of the advisor expressed and offered to shape the recipient's purposes. The outcome depends on whether counsel is received or rejected._
- **VCG-E-02** — _The inner forming of purposive schemes or counsel directed toward harming another person or group. The devising is deliberate, premeditated, and inner — formed in the heart before being enacted._
- **VCG-E-03** — _The inner purposing of the noble or morally oriented person — counsel as the outward expression of a sound inner character, including the case where the moral character is reflected back in what is planned._
- **VCG-E-04** — _God forms and executes sovereign intention that cannot be annulled or redirected. His counsel is self-originating, irresistible, and encompasses the whole of history. Multiple human terms (ya.ats, cha.shav, za.mam) converge in expressing this._
- **VCG-E-05** — _God forms purposive intent that is held open — the plan is real and announced, but its execution is conditional on human response. This is different from VCG-E-04 (irresistible) — here the divine intent can be withdrawn if the people turn._
- **VCG-E-06** — _The same event carries both human purposive intent (evil) and divine purposive intent (good) — the two work through each other. Gen 50:20 is the defining verse._
- **VCG-E-07** — _God forms purposive thought directed toward individual persons — specifically those who are poor, suffering, or needing — as an expression of attentive covenantal care._
- **VCG-E-08** — _God forms specific purposive plans for the welfare and future of his people — not reactive, not conditional, but a formed positive intent with named content (welfare, hope, future)._
- **VCG-E-09** — _The human inner will/desire forming an intent and moving toward action. Covers a wide range from trivial preferences to morally significant choices. The inner volitional act is what is named._
- **VCG-E-10** — _The inner purposive will of God or Christ — sovereign, self-originating, directing revelation, creation, gifts, and redemption. The will is not contingent on human response._
- **VCG-E-11** — _The inner weighing of options leading to a resolved decision — the mind deliberating and settling upon a course of action._
- **VCG-E-12** — _The inner will resolving upon a course of action specifically directed toward harming or killing another person._
- **VCG-E-13** — _A considered inner judgment or resolution — formed with deliberation and offered with authority, whether individual (apostolic judgment) or shared (communal purpose). The resolution is personal and accountable._
- **VCG-E-14** — _The act of setting a goal or purpose before the will — either human (a travel intention repeatedly frustrated) or divine (God setting forth Christ as propitiation from an eternal purpose)._
- **VCG-E-15** — _The capacity for purposeful foresight — either in governance (anticipating and providing for those under care) or in deliberate provision for desire (making plans to gratify inner want)._
- **VCG-E-16** — _The inner capacity for rational explanation and calculation — the mind seeking to understand the underlying structure of reality. Belongs to the living; ceases at death._
- **VCG-E-17** — _A single verse. The king's inner act of purposing and planning an appointment, disclosed as grounded in Daniel's excellent spirit._
- **VCG-E-18** — _A single verse. The captain appeals for the god to give thought to the crew — the hope that divine inner purposing will be directed toward those in need of rescue._
- **VCG-E-19** — _The inner-attending faculty deliberately directed and sustained — setting the heart to observe, consider, or take counsel within oneself. Produces learning, reorientation, and testimony._
- **VCG-E-20** — _The inner-attending faculty failing, collapsing, or being deliberately suppressed — the person who does not set their heart to what is before them._
- **VCG-E-21** — _The community deliberately gathering its collective will to form a shared purpose in response to a significant situation._
- **VCG-E-22** — _A human subject forms a purposeful intent and commits to carrying it out — the resolve of unified human purposing._

#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `749-001` → `VCG-E-01` (31 verses)

- **DB**: Counsel as wisdom given or received between persons, shaping inner orientation
- **NEW** (Human counsel: wisdom given between persons shaping deliberation): One person gives advice or counsel to another — the inner wisdom of the advisor expressed and offered to shape the recipient's purposes. The outcome depends on whether counsel is received or rejected.
- _Sample verse:_ Exo 18:19 (H3289)

##### `509-001` → `VCG-E-09` (21 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner act of human willing, intending, or desiring — the volitional faculty in motion toward an object or action
- **NEW** (Human volitional intent: boulomai naming purposive inner will in motion): The human inner will/desire forming an intent and moving toward action. Covers a wide range from trivial preferences to morally significant choices. The inner volitional act is what is named.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 1:19 (G1014)

##### `3334-001` → `VCG-E-02` (20 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the deliberate devising of harm — the inner formation of schemes, plots, or evil plans against another
- **NEW** (Hostile human counsel: devising harm through purposive inner planning against another): The inner forming of purposive schemes or counsel directed toward harming another person or group. The devising is deliberate, premeditated, and inner — formed in the heart before being enacted.
- _Sample verse:_ Neh 6:2 (H2803I)

##### `749-003` → `VCG-E-04` (10 verses)

- **DB**: Divine counsel as God's inner intentionality directed toward persons or nations
- **NEW** (Divine counsel: God's sovereign purposive intent directed toward nations and history): God forms and executes sovereign intention that cannot be annulled or redirected. His counsel is self-originating, irresistible, and encompasses the whole of history. Multiple human terms (ya.ats, cha.shav, za.mam) converge in expressing this.
- _Sample verse:_ Isa 14:24 (H3289)

##### `3334-002` → `VCG-E-05` (7 verses)

- **DB**: Term names purposive planning — the inner formation of a deliberate purpose or plan, whether by God or human agents
- **NEW** (Divine purposive planning with conditional openness to relenting): God forms purposive intent that is held open — the plan is real and announced, but its execution is conditional on human response. This is different from VCG-E-04 (irresistible) — here the divine intent can be withdrawn if the people turn.
- _Sample verse:_ Jer 18:8 (H2803I)

##### `749-002` → `VCG-E-02` (7 verses)

- **NEW** (Hostile human counsel: devising harm through purposive inner planning against another): The inner forming of purposive schemes or counsel directed toward harming another person or group. The devising is deliberate, premeditated, and inner — formed in the heart before being enacted.

- **DB**: Counsel as expression of inner moral character — noble, wicked, or hostile purposing
- **NEW** (Human counsel: wisdom given between persons shaping deliberation): One person gives advice or counsel to another — the inner wisdom of the advisor expressed and offered to shape the recipient's purposes. The outcome depends on whether counsel is received or rejected.
- _Sample verse:_ 2Ch 22:3 (H3289)

##### `754-001` → `VCG-E-21` (2 verses)

- **DB**: Deliberate inner purposing — planning together in response to a significant situation
- **NEW** (Communal deliberate purposing: uts as collective counsel-forming): The community deliberately gathering its collective will to form a shared purpose in response to a significant situation.
- _Sample verse:_ Judg 19:30 (H5779)

##### `3334-001` → `VCG-E-07` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the deliberate devising of harm — the inner formation of schemes, plots, or evil plans against another
- **NEW** (God's purposive care for the individual: divine inner attending and planning for the needy): God forms purposive thought directed toward individual persons — specifically those who are poor, suffering, or needing — as an expression of attentive covenantal care.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 40:17 (H2803I)

##### `3334-002` → `VCG-E-06` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names purposive planning — the inner formation of a deliberate purpose or plan, whether by God or human agents
- **NEW** (Purposive divine and human intent working through the same event toward opposite ends): The same event carries both human purposive intent (evil) and divine purposive intent (good) — the two work through each other. Gen 50:20 is the defining verse.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 50:20 (H2803I)

##### `3334-002` → `VCG-E-07` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names purposive planning — the inner formation of a deliberate purpose or plan, whether by God or human agents
- **NEW** (God's purposive care for the individual: divine inner attending and planning for the needy): God forms purposive thought directed toward individual persons — specifically those who are poor, suffering, or needing — as an expression of attentive covenantal care.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 40:17 (H2803I)

##### `3334-002` → `VCG-E-08` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names purposive planning — the inner formation of a deliberate purpose or plan, whether by God or human agents
- **NEW** (God's purposive planning for his people's welfare: the plans-for-welfare pattern): God forms specific purposive plans for the welfare and future of his people — not reactive, not conditional, but a formed positive intent with named content (welfare, hope, future).
- _Sample verse:_ Jer 29:11 (H2803I)

##### `3445-001` → `VCG-E-18` (1 verses)

- **DB**: The hope and cry that God would direct his thought toward persons in their need — the inner appeal for divine attention as a response to crisis (Jon 1:6).
- **NEW** (The appeal for divine purposive attending: a.shat as hope for divine attention in crisis): A single verse. The captain appeals for the god to give thought to the crew — the hope that divine inner purposing will be directed toward those in need of rescue.
- _Sample verse:_ Jon 1:6 (H6245B)

##### `3482-001` → `VCG-E-17` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Royal inner planning — the king's inner decisional act of planning an appointment, disclosing an excellent spirit as the basis
- **NEW** (Royal inner decisional planning: a.shit naming a king's purposive appointment): A single verse. The king's inner act of purposing and planning an appointment, disclosed as grounded in Daniel's excellent spirit.
- _Sample verse:_ Dan 6:3 (H6246)

##### `749-001` → `VCG-E-07` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Counsel as wisdom given or received between persons, shaping inner orientation
- **NEW** (God's purposive care for the individual: divine inner attending and planning for the needy): God forms purposive thought directed toward individual persons — specifically those who are poor, suffering, or needing — as an expression of attentive covenantal care.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 16:7 (H3289)

- **NEW** (God's purposive care for the individual: divine inner attending and planning for the needy): God forms purposive thought directed toward individual persons — specifically those who are poor, suffering, or needing — as an expression of attentive covenantal care.

- **NEW** (Human purposeful resolve: za.mam as intent formed and set out to achieve): A human subject forms a purposeful intent and commits to carrying it out — the resolve of unified human purposing.
- _Sample verse:_ Gen 11:6 (H2161)

### M15-F

_66 rows_

#### a. New VCGs derived (from v2)

| Code | Title | Verses |
|---|---|---:|
| `VCG-B-09` | Universal failure of human inner comprehension: suniēmi / asunetos | 1 |
| `VCG-F-01` | Meditative dwelling on God's works and mighty acts: si.ach as sustained inner pondering | 5 |
| `VCG-F-02` | Meditative dwelling on God's law, precepts, and word: si.ach as law-meditation | 7 |
| `VCG-F-03` | All-day sustained meditation as the ground of understanding: si.chah | 3 |
| `VCG-F-04` | Complaint and lament as inner distress voiced: si.ach as outward expression of suffering | 3 |
| `VCG-F-05` | Telling/proclaiming of God's wondrous works: si.ach turned outward | 3 |
| `VCG-F-06` | Inner musing that burns to groaning and speech: ha.gig as prayer-substance | 2 |
| `VCG-F-07` | Heart-meditation producing understanding: ha.gut as the contemplative inner engagement | 1 |
| `VCG-F-08` | Heart-meditation offered to God alongside spoken words: hig.ga.von as worship substance | 2 |
| `VCG-F-09` | Focused contemplative attention directed at a revelatory vision: se.khal | 1 |
| `VCG-F-10` | God declaring the inner thought of the human person: se.ach | 1 |
| `VCG-F-11` | Evil thoughts arising from the heart: dialogismos as corrupt inner reasoning | 5 |
| `VCG-F-12` | Disputed opinions, doubts, and inner questioning: dialogismos as contested inner deliberation | 10 |
| `VCG-F-13` | Individual inner reasoning and questioning: dialogizomai as the heart deliberating with itself | 6 |
| `VCG-F-14` | Communal shared deliberation: dialogizomai as reasoning together | 4 |
| `VCG-F-15` | Inner conceived thoughts perceived by Jesus or exposed by the word: enthumēsis | 5 |
| `VCG-F-16` | Deliberate inner reflection on a situation: enthumeomai as considered attending | 2 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-B-09** — _The total absence of inner understanding in fallen humanity — not a specific judicial act but a description of the general human condition before God._
- **VCG-F-01** — _The person turns inward attention to God's past acts — creation, history, deliverance, wondrous works — and dwells upon them. The attention is sustained, intentional, and productive of awe or orientation._
- **VCG-F-02** — _The sustained inward dwelling on God's law, precepts, statutes, and promises — the defining meditative practice of the devoted person. The object is always divine instruction. All uses from Psalm 119._
- **VCG-F-03** — _Sustained, all-day meditative engagement with God's testimonies as the practice that produces understanding — more than teachers can give._
- **VCG-F-04** — _The inner dwelling on distress that finds outward expression in complaint, moaning, or lament. The si.ach is the voicing of what has been turned over inwardly._
- **VCG-F-05** — _The meditative inner dwelling on God's wondrous works turns outward into proclamation — the result of meditation is speech that tells what God has done._
- **VCG-F-06** — _Deep inner reflective engagement that intensifies inwardly — becoming fire in the heart — and is then offered to God as the substance of prayer._
- **VCG-F-07** — _A single verse. The meditation of the heart is named as what produces understanding — the reflective inner engagement before God is the generative activity from which wisdom flows._
- **VCG-F-08** — _The heart's meditative activity offered to God as the inward counterpart of spoken prayer — what the mouth says and what the heart meditates are both presented._
- **VCG-F-09** — _A single verse. The focused, careful attending to what is seen in a prophetic vision — a deliberate inner act of considering what appears._
- **VCG-F-10** — _A single verse. God knows and declares to man what his thought is — the creative God who forms mountains also knows and discloses the inner thought of the creature._
- **VCG-F-11** — _The evil reasoning or thoughts that originate in the heart — not incidental but structural, preceding and generating sinful action. They are the inner source of moral failure._
- **VCG-F-12** — _The inner reasoning that is in dispute — either doubts arising in the heart that disturb faith, or contested opinions that produce quarrelling within the community._
- **VCG-F-13** — _The inner act of the individual person reasoning within themselves — the heart raising questions, forming impressions, or trying to understand. Can be neutral, perplexed, or in the presence of Jesus._
- **VCG-F-14** — _The disciples or others reasoning together as a group — discussing a shared situation, usually producing an inadequate response that Jesus addresses._
- **VCG-F-15** — _The inner conceived thoughts of persons — the cognitive acts of the heart — that are directly accessible to Christ's perception or to the living word of God._
- **VCG-F-16** — _The deliberate inner act of reflecting upon and considering a situation — sustained, purposive attending that precedes a decision or response._

#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `1081-002` → `VCG-F-12` (9 verses)

- **DB**: Term names inner doubts, arguments, or disputed opinions — the mind's questioning and deliberating about contested matters
- **NEW** (Disputed opinions, doubts, and inner questioning: dialogismos as contested inner deliberation): The inner reasoning that is in dispute — either doubts arising in the heart that disturb faith, or contested opinions that produce quarrelling within the community.
- _Sample verse:_ Luk 2:35 (G1261)

##### `242-001` → `VCG-F-02` (7 verses)

- **DB**: Meditation and inner pondering — reflective contemplation of God's works and word
- **NEW** (Meditative dwelling on God's law, precepts, and word: si.ach as law-meditation): The sustained inward dwelling on God's law, precepts, statutes, and promises — the defining meditative practice of the devoted person. The object is always divine instruction. All uses from Psalm 119.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 119:15 (H7878)

##### `1184-001` → `VCG-F-13` (6 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner act of reasoning or questioning — the mind deliberating with itself or the heart raising doubts and questions
- **NEW** (Individual inner reasoning and questioning: dialogizomai as the heart deliberating with itself): The inner act of the individual person reasoning within themselves — the heart raising questions, forming impressions, or trying to understand. Can be neutral, perplexed, or in the presence of Jesus.
- _Sample verse:_ Mar 2:6 (G1260)

##### `1081-001` → `VCG-F-11` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the evil thoughts that originate in the heart — the corrupt inner reasoning that produces sin and estrangement from God
- **NEW** (Evil thoughts arising from the heart: dialogismos as corrupt inner reasoning): The evil reasoning or thoughts that originate in the heart — not incidental but structural, preceding and generating sinful action. They are the inner source of moral failure.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 15:19 (G1261)

##### `242-001` → `VCG-F-01` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Meditation and inner pondering — reflective contemplation of God's works and word
- **NEW** (Meditative dwelling on God's works and mighty acts: si.ach as sustained inner pondering): The person turns inward attention to God's past acts — creation, history, deliverance, wondrous works — and dwells upon them. The attention is sustained, intentional, and productive of awe or orientation.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 77:3 (H7878)

##### `1184-002` → `VCG-F-14` (4 verses)

- _Sample verse:_ Mat 16:7 (G1260)

##### `917-001` → `VCG-F-15` (4 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner cognitive act of conception — the thoughts and devisings of the heart, both as the inner content that Christ perceives and God's word discerns, and as the inner faculty by which a person forms conceptions (including, where misdirected, conceptions of God)
- **NEW** (Inner conceived thoughts perceived by Jesus or exposed by the word: enthumēsis): The inner conceived thoughts of persons — the cognitive acts of the heart — that are directly accessible to Christ's perception or to the living word of God.
- _Sample verse:_ Mat 9:4 (G1761)

- **NEW** (All-day sustained meditation as the ground of understanding: si.chah): Sustained, all-day meditative engagement with God's testimonies as the practice that produces understanding — more than teachers can give.

### M15-G

_27 rows_

#### a. New VCGs derived (from v2)

| Code | Title | Verses |
|---|---|---:|
| `VCG-G-01` | Knowledge as inner capacity for wise governance and discernment: mad.da | 5 |
| `VCG-G-02` | Inner consciousness as the moral seat: mad.da as thought-life | 1 |
| `VCG-G-03` | Thoughts alarmed by revelatory dream-visions: ra.yon | 6 |
| `VCG-G-04` | Inner thoughts known by God and precious to the psalmist: re.a | 2 |
| `VCG-G-05` | Ease-induced inner contempt for suffering: ash.tut | 1 |
| `VCG-G-06` | Plans and thoughts that perish at death: esh.to.nah as mortality marker | 1 |
| `VCG-G-07` | The inner cognitive faculty as site of spiritual contest: noēma | 6 |
| `VCG-G-08` | The faculty of mature thinking: frēn | 1 |
| `VCG-G-09` | Inner thoughts and purposes of the heart; the way of thinking to be adopted: ennoia | 2 |
| `VCG-G-10` | The purposeful inner intent of the heart requiring repentance: epinoia | 1 |
| `VCG-G-11` | Hidden inner thoughts known directly to Jesus: dianoēma | 1 |

_Descriptions:_

- **VCG-G-01** — _Mad.da names the formed knowledge held within that equips the person for a task — specifically governance and discernment. The knowledge is requested, given by God, and enables wise leadership._
- **VCG-G-02** — _Mad.da used for the thought-life or inner consciousness as the place where private moral evaluation occurs — even private thoughts carry accountability._
- **VCG-G-03** — _Inner thought-content produced in response to divine revelation through dreams or visions — in every case the ra.yon disturbs or alarms the person receiving or hearing of it. Includes the thoughts the queen counsels the king not to allow to master him._
- **VCG-G-04** — _The psalmist's thoughts are transparent to God, discerned from afar. God's own thoughts are precious and vast beyond counting. The same word applies in both directions, creating a symmetry of mutual thought-content._
- **VCG-G-05** — _A single verse. The inner attitude of those who are comfortable — from their ease, they form inner contempt for those whose feet slip into misfortune._
- **VCG-G-06** — _A single verse. The inner purposings and plans of a person belong to the living — on the day their breath departs, these plans perish. Inner thought-content is constitutively linked to life._
- **VCG-G-07** — _The mind as inner cognitive faculty is not neutral — it can be hardened, blinded, led astray, or guarded. Satan works through it; God guards it; the apostolic mission takes its thoughts captive. All six uses locate noēma as a contested inner terrain._
- **VCG-G-08** — _A single verse. The capacity for moral and rational discernment — named as a faculty that can be childlike or mature. The command is to be mature in this faculty while being infants in evil._
- **VCG-G-09** — _The inner thought-content and purposive orientation of the heart — what only God's word can discern (Heb 4:12), and the way of thinking to be taken on as armour (1Pe 4:1)._
- **VCG-G-10** — _A single verse. The inner thought-disposition that animated Simon's attempt to purchase the Spirit — a purposeful intent that requires repentance and forgiveness._
- **VCG-G-11** — _A single verse. The hidden inner thought-content of persons that is directly accessible to Jesus's perception — he knows what they are thinking before they speak._

#### f. Side-by-side text comparison (one pair per DB↔NEW flow)

##### `1188-001` → `VCG-G-07` (6 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner faculty of thought — the mind's contents and its susceptibility to hardening, blinding, or corrupting by spiritual forces
- **NEW** (The inner cognitive faculty as site of spiritual contest: noēma): The mind as inner cognitive faculty is not neutral — it can be hardened, blinded, led astray, or guarded. Satan works through it; God guards it; the apostolic mission takes its thoughts captive. All six uses locate noēma as a contested inner terrain.
- _Sample verse:_ 2Cor 2:11 (G3540)

##### `3449-001` → `VCG-G-03` (6 verses)

- **DB**: Thoughts alarmed by revelation — the inner mental content produced by dream-visions that disturbs the person's inner state, including the thoughts the king is urged not to let alarm him and Daniel's thoughts kept in the heart
- **NEW** (Thoughts alarmed by revelatory dream-visions: ra.yon): Inner thought-content produced in response to divine revelation through dreams or visions — in every case the ra.yon disturbs or alarms the person receiving or hearing of it. Includes the thoughts the queen counsels the king not to allow to master him.
- _Sample verse:_ Dan 2:29 (H7476)

##### `960-001` → `VCG-G-01` (5 verses)

- **DB**: Knowledge as inner capacity for wise governance and discernment
- **NEW** (Knowledge as inner capacity for wise governance and discernment: mad.da): Mad.da names the formed knowledge held within that equips the person for a task — specifically governance and discernment. The knowledge is requested, given by God, and enables wise leadership.
- _Sample verse:_ 2Ch 1:10 (H4093)

##### `3372-001` → `VCG-G-09` (2 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner thoughts and purposes of the heart — the hidden intentional life that only God's word can discern and expose
- **NEW** (Inner thoughts and purposes of the heart; the way of thinking to be adopted: ennoia): The inner thought-content and purposive orientation of the heart — what only God's word can discern (Heb 4:12), and the way of thinking to be taken on as armour (1Pe 4:1).
- _Sample verse:_ Heb 4:12 (G1771)

##### `3453-001` → `VCG-G-04` (2 verses)

- **DB**: Thoughts known to and held by God — the inner thoughts of persons discerned by God from afar, and God's own thoughts precious to the psalmist
- **NEW** (Inner thoughts known by God and precious to the psalmist: re.a): The psalmist's thoughts are transparent to God, discerned from afar. God's own thoughts are precious and vast beyond counting. The same word applies in both directions, creating a symmetry of mutual thought-content.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 139:2 (H7454)

##### `1178-001` → `VCG-G-05` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Ease-induced inner contempt — the thought or inner attitude of those at ease that generates contempt for the suffering of others
- **NEW** (Ease-induced inner contempt for suffering: ash.tut): A single verse. The inner attitude of those who are comfortable — from their ease, they form inner contempt for those whose feet slip into misfortune.
- _Sample verse:_ Job 12:5 (H6248)

##### `2493-001` → `VCG-G-08` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the faculty of mature thinking — the capacity for moral and rational discernment that marks adult inner life
- **NEW** (The faculty of mature thinking: frēn): A single verse. The capacity for moral and rational discernment — named as a faculty that can be childlike or mature. The command is to be mature in this faculty while being infants in evil.
- _Sample verse:_ 1Cor 14:20 (G5424)

##### `3375-001` → `VCG-G-10` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Term names the inner thought or intent of the heart — the purposeful inner disposition that orients a person's actions, here in the context of moral failure requiring repentance
- **NEW** (The purposeful inner intent of the heart requiring repentance: epinoia): A single verse. The inner thought-disposition that animated Simon's attempt to purchase the Spirit — a purposeful intent that requires repentance and forgiveness.
- _Sample verse:_ Act 8:22 (G1963)

##### `3408-001` → `VCG-G-11` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Hidden inner thoughts perceived and known by Jesus — the inner cognitive content of persons directly accessible to divine perception
- **NEW** (Hidden inner thoughts known directly to Jesus: dianoēma): A single verse. The hidden inner thought-content of persons that is directly accessible to Jesus's perception — he knows what they are thinking before they speak.
- _Sample verse:_ Luk 11:17 (G1270)

##### `3442-001` → `VCG-G-06` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Plans that perish at death — the inner thoughts and purposes that cease when the person dies, disclosing the fragility of inner purposing
- **NEW** (Plans and thoughts that perish at death: esh.to.nah as mortality marker): A single verse. The inner purposings and plans of a person belong to the living — on the day their breath departs, these plans perish. Inner thought-content is constitutively linked to life.
- _Sample verse:_ Psa 146:4 (H6250)

##### `960-002` → `VCG-G-02` (1 verses)

- **DB**: Thought-life or inner consciousness as moral seat of the person
- **NEW** (Inner consciousness as the moral seat: mad.da as thought-life): Mad.da used for the thought-life or inner consciousness as the place where private moral evaluation occurs — even private thoughts carry accountability.
- _Sample verse:_ Ecc 10:20 (H4093)

### 4.3 Duplicate active verse_context rows (2 vr_ids)

_These vr_ids each have 2 active vc rows in the DB — must be resolved before any sub-group cleanup._

| vr_id | Reference | Strongs | Sub-group | DB VCGs (two of them) |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 130804 | Psa 40:17 | H2803I cha.shav | `M15-E` | 3334-001, 3334-002 |
